--- 帖子 #1 ---
Hello traders and welcome to the wonderful world of Wolfe waves!

This thread is meant to be a place where newbies and/or experienced professionals can come together to share, learn, and encourage.

The rules are simple: Be respectful and professional. Anything less won't be tolerated.

Before we get started, I would like to acknowledge Bill Wolfe, the founder of Wolfe wave analysis. I am grateful to have stumbled upon his work. A quick overview can be found here:  Attached File(s)   Wolfe-Wave-book (1) (3).pdf

7.8 MB
|
25,253 downloads

If you're a struggling trader, frustrated and ready to give up, or just an all out system hopping, account blowing, psychotic indicator junkie, then this strategy just might be the perfect antidote for your trading endeavors. Or, if you are a seasoned professional, this strategy might simply be a nice addition to your trading tool box. In either case, Wolfe wave analysis provides a mechanically simplistic method to enter a trade in the so called "sweet zone". These trades have a high probability of success. In addition, the very nature of the Wolfe wave structure allows you to mitigate your risk through very well defined stop loss areas.

Just to clarify up front, I don't claim to be a Wolfe wave guru. Most of what I have learned has come from pouring over 1000's of charts for the past 6 months. There are a few free online resources, but other than regurgitating the basic wave structure along with a fleeting mention of the sweet zone, I haven't seen any real discussion as to how you locate the best price to enter into the trade. Do you enter at the trend line break, half way into the sweet zone, at the bottom of the sweet zone, or do you wait for a clear reversal with some sort of confirmation tool? This is the paramount question that we are trying to answer.

For ease of discussion the following acronyms will be used:

WW = WOLFE WAVE
CWW = CLASSIC WOLFE WAVE
HWW = HORIZONTAL WOLFE WAVE

I think it's best to fully delve into the CWW structure first before discussing the HWW.
I put this diagram together as a quick reference as to what constitutes a valid CWW.

Note: I use XABCD to describe the wave instead of the normal 12345. The reason being is that most traders are likely very familiar with the AB=CD concept and it is an important tool used here in determining the entry price for our trades.

HERE IS THE CLASSIC WOLFE WAVE STRUCTURE
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

The Sweet Zone

In my opinion, the sweet zone is the most important part of the Wolfe Wave trading strategy. It baffles me that traders rarely discuss this topic. Understanding the parameters of the sweet zone is paramount to getting the best possible entry price. Sweet zones can be anywhere from 3 to 300 pips depending on the steepness of the wave and/or the time frame being traded. So the question is, where do I enter the trade? What criteria should I use? What tools should I use? And where should my stop loss be placed? I'm glad you asked. These questions and more will be discussed in detail as we progress forward in our study.

Let me make an analogy that I find pertinent to this discussion. Hopefully most traders here are familiar with Major League Baseball. In my opinion, trading in the sweet zone is very similar to a major league hitter when he gets into the batter's box. If you talk to a professional baseball player about hitting, they will tell you that their main objective is to hit the ball hard. It doesn't matter where the ball ends up or if they make an out, their goal is to hit the ball hard? How do you hit the ball hard. Well, you make sure you make contact on the "sweet" spot of the baseball bat. How do you do that?

Preparation and patience - Make sure your cleats are clean. Make sure your bat isn't cracked. Make sure your gloves are in good condition. Make sure you know as much about the opposing pitcher as possible in advance. What kind of pitches does he throw? What's his "go-to" pitch? What kind of release angle does he have? Side arm? Over the top? How has he pitched you in the past? What stage of the game are we in? Are there runners on base? Is he showing signs of exhaustion? Having considered all of those things, the hitter will try and "wait" for "his" pitch. By being prepared, patient and cognizant of all of the pertinent information around him, he is then in a good position to try and force the pitcher to throw a pitch that is right in his sweet zone. And when that happens, the odds will be stacked in his favor. You get the point I'm sure.

Do your due diligence and be patient. Let the price come into your sweet zone. Make sure your working area is prepared. Make sure your mind is prepared. Make sure you have mapped out all of your potential trades in advance. A hitter stepping into the batter's box is the same as a trader who is monitoring price action as it approaches the sweet zone. If he isn't prepared, he might not hit the ball very hard. In fact, he might even strike out. If we as traders aren't prepared we may miss the sweet zone or worse yet, strike out altogether.

If a hitter makes contact with the sweet spot on the bat and makes an out, he may be disappointed, but he knows that he has done his job. Maybe he smacked a one hop sizzler only to see the second baseman make a spectacular diving play. Or maybe he hit a line drive right on the sweet spot that went directly towards the left fielder for and easy out. It doesn't matter, he did his job, he hit the ball hard right on the sweet spot. He may be frustrated at that moment, but a true professional knows that eventually, the hits will come, the runs score, the production will increase.

In the same way, a trader's only objective is to "hit" the trade right on the sweet spot. Maybe the trade failed because of a surprise news event, or a low liquidity stop loss run. Maybe the trade failed for reasons we can't explain. So be it, we can analyze what may have gone wrong and add that knowledge to our mental toolbox for the next time we step into the batter's box. As long as we poured every bit of due diligence and discipline into entering that trade at the best possible price within the sweet zone, then we have done our job. We know that over time the winners will come, the pips will pile up, the accounts will grow.

EXIT STRATEGY

Every good entry needs a good exit. Below is my mechanical exit strategy ( I like to divide my positions up into 3 equal parts). I use the X, C, and A points as my reference points for exit. It is likely that there will be an increase in price action at these points just based on the nature of S/R. I would actually be setting my TP levels 5-20 pips below these three levels based on the time frame. I am generally very conservative with my TP's. I don't want to set my TP right at the level only to see price reverse significantly without banking some pips.

Note: When price reaches TP #1 just shy of level X, then the SL's for the two remaining positions are moved to BE.

Note: There is no short cut to becoming proficient in trading Wolfe waves or trading any other method for that matter. I believe it's imperative that traders take the time to learn how to draw Wolfe waves manually. Having a working knowledge of the structure and the ability to spot them on your own will go a long way towards improving your results. Having said that, this indicator is simply fantastic. It's so versatile and user friendly. As you read through the thread (and I hope you do), you will see how many modifications and improvements have been made. This will give you a strong skill set in knowing how to use this indicator to your advantage. Please understand that this indicator will find many many WWs. You will find waves with excellent symmetry and some with horrible symmetry. Some waves will be very steep angled and others will be nearly horizontal. It's your job to sift through these waves and find those that offer the best potential. Well structured waves with several layers of confluence are the diamonds in the rough and offer the highest probability for success.

FILTERING YOUR TRADES: POST #1286

Please feel free to post your charts with any questions. I am here to learn just as much as you are. Maybe you have some good filters to share with us or different parameters when entering a trade. We are all in this together. My hope is that "iron will sharpen iron" and that the end result will be a growing group of seasoned Wolfe wave gurus.

FINAL THOUGHTS

WWs work on all pairs, time frames, and instruments. WWs are often the endpoints of other larger more complex harmonic structures. I have noticed that pairs and the market in general tend to go through harmonic phases. Set ups seem to be developing everywhere. Other times, price action looks like a gazelle running away from a cheetah.

Be especially careful when trading volatile pairs on smaller time frames. Trying to trade the GBP/NZD on a 5 minute time frame during low liquidity with a 5 pip spread isn't very prudent. There are many set ups every day so there is no need to force a trade during these high risk scenarios.

Be mindful of news events. Active trades on smaller time frames are very susceptible to spikes and widening spreads.

When monitoring your active trade, be cognizant of any smaller WWs that are developing inside the bigger wave. These smaller waves could give you a clue that it is time to bag the pips and manually end your trade.

But most of all, make sure you are enjoying the chase. Trading is hard work and can be frustrating at times. For me, the best feeling in the world is stalking, executing, and then winning the trade. Trading is my job and I absolutely love to go to work!!

"A problem is merely an opportunity to find a solution"

What follows are a couple of initial examples of CWW's with accompanying explanations as to how I determined what would be the most prudent sweet zone entry price.

--- 帖子 #2 ---
Pictured below is a CWW that exhibits near perfect symmetry. What I mean by that is that AB and CD are nearly the same length in pips. In addition, both legs took exactly 12 candles to complete. That's all fine and dandy, but the problem still remains; where do we enter our trade?

If you look at where the trend line is broken compared to where the bottom of the sweet zone is, well, that's about 100 pips. Even though this is a 4H TF, that's still looks like a lot of potential risk. If we enter at the trend line our SL would have to be upwards of 150 pips which is completely unacceptable. So what do we do?

The first thing I do is map out the wave. After some chart time, the developing waves will jump off the screen at you. When you see a wave entering the D leg, map it out. In that way, you will already know in advance exactly where you are going to scale in, provided the structure is still valid when and if price reaches that zone.

MAPPING OUT THE WAVE

1)Draw the red trend line, the green target line, the yellow trend line and the other yellow parallel extension line. Use the diagram in post 1 for a reference.

2)Put the XABCD points on the chart in the appropriate spots. It may seem silly to do this as you already know where those spots are, but for me its about due diligence and complete visual clarity, especially when teaching, discussing, or learning from others

3)Using the zigzag indicator, find and mark the AB=CD completion level.

4)Put the BC fib extension on your chart. You'll be surprised how many times the AB=CD completion level matches up perfectly with one of the fib levels.

5)Given the TF that you're in, look back an appropriate distance in time to locate any previous zones of critical S/R and mark them as rectangular zones

6)I don't use them but some people like to have a look at the Bollinger bands.

Not always, but as a general rule, you will notice these repeating patterns:

1) WWs with flatter angles tend to reverse at the 113 or 127 fib extensions
2) WWs with moderate angles tend to reverse at the 141 or 161 fib extensions
3) WWs with extremely steep angles tend to reverse at the 200 to 261 fib extensions

Obviously there is going to be some subjectivity in determining exactly where the entry price is going to be, but with more and more chart time you will become extremely confident in your entry point.

In the example below, I didn't find any previous S/R that lined up with the sweet zone but the fact that AB=CD landed right on the 161 fib made it a no brainer. Either scale in with very small positions starting at the 141 fib down to the 161 fib, or wait until price is much closer to the 161 fib and scale in with fewer larger sized positions. In both cases the SL is going to be at least half way to the 200 fib (depending on risk parameters, SL could also be below the 200 fib).

Bottom line: By doing our homework in advance, we have mitigated our risk substantially. Of course this example is a cherry picked winner, but ultimately it was a 400 pip move to the target line with a SL as little as 50-100 pips depending on the risk management parameters.

Note: Bill Wolfe was trading stocks and equities when he founded his wave theory and as such had access to true market volume. He noted that volume should spike up at the point of reversal. This makes sense as most reversal areas are basically a battle between bulls and bears. Unfortunately, forex broker volume isn't necessarily indicative of true market volume. Still, on occasion I will have a look at the MFI (Bill Wiiliams market facilitation index) just to see what's going on in the retail world

CAD/JPY 4H CLASSIC WOLFE WAVE (CWW)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Zooming in to the hourly chart illustrates the challenge we face in deciding where to enter the trade. If you notice on the way down to the ultimate reversal point, there are two price bounces of about 50 pips each. If we had entered at the original trend line break, then where would our stop be placed? Likewise, if we entered at the second bounce, where would our SL be? Also, check out the TDI indicator at the bottom. It's very choppy as price is heading down to the true reversal price. Point being, the AB=CD makes this problem go away. We might miss the trade if price never reaches that point, but we have mitigated our risk substantially.

This also brings up another point, and that is, why don't we just wait for a TDI cross and then enter the trade. A Valid point and there is nothing wrong with doing that. The only difference is your SL will be greater, especially on the higher time frames.

--- 帖子 #3 ---
This example doesn't exhibit the same symmetry. Price ultimately reversed about 46 pips before AB=CD completion. That's not really too much considering this is on the daily TF.

Anyways, we go ahead and map it out. As is often the case the AB=CD ended right about at the 161 fib. Again, we have the same problem. We have about 140 pips from the TL break to the bottom of the sweet zone to contend with. Do we jump in at the 127 fib? Maybe we scale in at the 141? Well, before making that decision I zoomed out and noticed some very distinct previous S/R. Take a look at the second chart to see what I mean. Problem solved. I either scale in from the 127 fib or wait until price gets near the 141 fib and scale in with fewer larger positions. SL below the 161 fib. Only a 50-80 pip SL for a move that eventually ended up being about 500 pips. Of course, all in hindsight and likely would have taken some profits off the table on the way up, but a pretty good RR nonetheless.

WTI CRUDE 15MIN CCW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

This chart is self explanatory. All of our levels are right in front of our eyes. Previous S/R tells us that there is likely going to be a battle in the sweet zone. We can see the whole field now. All we have to do now is monitor price action and wait for the moment to strike. Price may never actually make it to the sweet zone, or the wave structure might become invalid. In either case, so be it. We just scrap the plan and look to map out other developing waves.

--- 帖子 #23 ---
If I understand your first question correctly, I will enter the trade without waiting to see if there is any reversal. I'm assuming in advance, based on the WW structure, AB=CD completion, and the previous S/R that there WILL be a reaction at the price I have marked.

I know most traders would rather wait to see a reversal get started. Many times price will bounce off the preset level then retest that level. If I wait for price to bounce 10 pips now my SL will have to be 20 pips. If price eventually break through and continues higher, I have basically doubled my loss. I'd rather enter first with the 10 pip SL rather than wait for any confirmation. In essence, for me, the conformation IS the Wolfe wave itself coupled with all of the other layers of confluence.

Im not sure if that answers your question.

The UJ set up is not a valid WW because line XB does not converge with line AC (refer to the diagram posted on page one). Even if it was, I would rather stay away from that potential set up anyways. Terrible symmetry, large re trace before leg D completes, just doesn't fit any of the valid WW structure

Anyways, thanks for the post.

A little friendly advice. That PVSRA chart and system is a work of art. I have read thru a lot of Cigarguy's posts, excellent trader with a great system. But for our purposes here, it is best to start with a naked chart. The only thing on my chart initially is the price and the zigzag. Then just map it out. After enough practice you'll  see right away that a certain pattern doesn't fit the WW structure

--- 帖子 #29 ---
In order to get better at understanding of what works, it's important to look at what doesn't work.

Three reasons NOT to take this trade

1) No symmetry at all
2) No previous S/R confluence
3) AB=CD completion with no FIB confluence

Right off the bat you can see AB moves 124 pips in 2 candles while CD just plods along actually bouncing off the trend line for like 50 candles to make it's 124 pips to completion. When it reaches completion, you see a little congestion, then ultimately price breaks thru 50 pips higher, far to much for a SL on 30 minutes.

In addition, just look at how the zig zag is moving. Its all over the place. There is nothing harmonic about the price action on the entire chart.

Hi Jack.

I couldn't really give you a success rate as that really depends on the person and their ability to find the best set ups. What I can say is that the WW strategy gives the "edge" that we need to be successful in this business.

The 3 drive pattern is a different animal in my opinion mainly because their are no trend line breaks. It's more like trading channels. The WW pattern theory is based on the fact that the "physics" of the wave is out of balance at the trend line break and that their will be an equal an opposite reaction to re-balance the larger wave or system if you will.

--- 帖子 #62 ---
It's important to remember that the AB=CD doesn't have to necessarily complete to validate an entry. I map it out just to know where it is, and to see if it is going to show confluence with the structure as a whole. In fact, It may be in Bill Wolfe's course but he never mentioned it in the pdf overview. Also, I have never seen anyone else mention the AB=CD as an entry requirement, it was just something I added as a potential filter.

If you look at that daily CHF/JPY set up it shows very nice symmetry. AB = 7 CANDLES CD = 6 CANDLES.

For price to have reached the completion on candle 7, 8 or even 9, it would have had to entirely break through the bottom extension line XB of the sweet zone, which to my mind would invalidate the structure. Like I said, this is still a work in progress and these are excellent talking points. Also, this IS the daily so it is reasonable to expect that the AB=CD won't be exact. This trade is very similar to the NU daily I posted (post#3).

On the flip side, this is a good scenario for our earlier discussion about entering after the reversal. In hindsight of course, but entering after the reversal on the TDI cross would have worked out well. Again, the AB=CD was put in place to try and mitigate risk. In this case, based on the price hitting XB, in would be acceptable to scale in at the 161FIB (which happens to be near the testing of the 200EMA). A quick look at Bollinger bands shows price had pierced the bottom level as well. We certainly dont want to force any trade but in this instance there may have been other factors to consider other than ABCD.

Just my rant, off to the movies, back tonight

--- 帖子 #75 ---
Not really a feeling, more of a mechanics thing.

The definitive characteristic of this wave is how flat it is. Notice XB is almost horizontal and given that AB was a swift and smooth 7 candle move it negates any possibility of CD completing with symmetry inside the sweet zone. The only way CD can complete is to slowly ride down the extension line, in which case there could be no symmetry with AB.

Basically we are on the verge of the a parallel Wolfe wave (PWW), which I intentionally left out for now just because it brings in a whole other set of entry strategies. Honestly, I am still studying the PWWs. Hopefully later on that is something we can get into, but for now just trying to master the classic wave.

Remember, mechanically speaking the sweet zone is anywhere from the XB trend line to the AC parallel extension line. Entry strategies are subjective and vary greatly form one trader to the next.

--- 帖子 #79 ---
If you look at the entry (first) post it says:

EXIT STRATEGY

Every good entry needs a good exit. Below is my mechanical exit strategy ( I like to divide my positions up into 3 equal parts). I use the X, C, and A points as my reference points for exit. It is likely that there will be an increase in price action at these points just based on the nature of S/R. I would actually be setting my TP levels 5-20 pips below these three levels based on the time frame. I am generally very conservative with my TP's. I don't want to set my TP right at the level only to see price reverse significantly without bagging some pips.

Note: When price reaches TP #1 just shy of level X, then the SL's for the two remaining positions are moved to BE.

In regards to your specific pattern I would most likely take the final profit at around 1:6RR as the 1-4 line is very steep

--- 帖子 #87 ---
AB=CD is not 100% necessary for entry. It is always good to know where that level is, especially for waves that have steep angles.

If you are unsure about entry, the completion level is potentially a good spot, especially if there is confluence with previous S/R, fibos, 200EMA, etc

Also, it is important to note that most traders that trade reversal patterns of any kind tend to wait for confirmation and don't enter until a reversal candle has completed. Perfectly acceptable. Entries are subjective and will vary from trader to trader based on their risk tolerance, personality, and trading style.

The one thing that's generally ALWAYS true is that entry takes place inside the "sweet" zone.

--- 帖子 #93 ---
Waves #2 and #5 that you posted don't fit any wave we will be studying here.

Waves #1 and #3 do not fit the requirements of a Classic Wolfe wave (CWW), because lines XB and AC don't converge.

Ironically, #1 and #3 are what I call an "Anti" Wolfe wave (AWW) that I kind of made up during my study period. In my first post I mentioned that we might discuss this type of wave after getting a good grasp on the classic wave. I just didn't want traders to get confused. I would of actually traded your set up as a valid Anti Wolfe wave (AWW).

Three differences that the Anti Wolfe wave exhibit:

1) Lines XB and AC do NOT converge

2) Price rarely gets to far into the "anti" sweet zone, if you will, just because of the "expanding" nature of the wave.

3) Because of difference 2, the entry generally takes place very near the AB=CD completion and very near to the parallel extension line.

Wave #4 is actually a Parallel Wolfe wave (PWW) which we haven't discussed yet either. Line XB is horizontal which is what defines the parallel wave

By the way, THANK YOU for using the template and for marking out the points so clearly. It makes the discussion so much easier for everyone involved, especially me.

Cheers

Here is an Anti wave example that I had saved for a discussion at a later date. Note how is looks almost exactly like yours. it also shows a classic wave developing near the TP zone as a good indicator for exit

First let me preface by stating that I took Bill Wolfe's course,

was trained by him in the methodology, and have corresponded

with him regarding setups. I do not mean to rain on anyone's

parade, but many of the charts being offered here as Wolfe Waves

are the farthest thing from them.  If the "Street Smarts" book, or

a knock-off website is your only exposure to this setup, then it is

very unlikely that you are trading Wolfe Waves properly. And over

the long haul, your results will bear this out.

--- 帖子 #132 ---
Conventional wisdom says wait for the TDI cross then put your stop above the original price spike. I do that sometimes, but usually I am entering as price hits my predetermined zone.

I am trying to get more bang for my buck out of the entry (closer to the ultimate spike). In this case price only advanced 11 pips past the AB=CD level, not bad for an hourly set up. Waiting for the TDI cross is fine, you'll just have to decide if you want your SL to be above the last printed candle or much higher above the original price spike, which in the is case over 20 pips.

Once you get more confidence in the structure and set up, you will start to get more comfortable with the entry. A lot depends on your risk management profile. Either way, its important to know what SL level  is going to give your trade reasonable breathing room without exposing yourself to too much risk.

.

and move to a larger or smaller time frame based on what you observe?  How many

--- 帖子 #181 ---

--- 帖子 #182 ---
Edit: Sorry, I missed that you wanted Expo's way of finding them. Feel free to read mine below!

Sure. If using the uploaded ZigZag indicator, the first step is to look for channel-like structures with converging trendlines (looking like the drawn images in the first post). If you find them, see if they fit the rules in the first post (for instance for a bearish setup the lower trendline needs to be steeper). Then map out the b-c line, fibonacci extension and the ABCD pattern to find the sweetzone. It's all in the first post.

The timeframe doesn't matter, we are only learning the pattern here. When finding the pattern we do not need to have multiple charts open either. I have two lists of pairs that I get lower spread on from my broker, and so they are better when trading 5-15 min patterns. For 30-min plus I scan almost all pairs (with all I mean the major crosses, it's about 20). I do this when I have time, about 2-4 times a day. It only takes a couple of minutes.

When we have found the setups we can start look at other things to filter them. We can look at different timeframes, RSI, divergence, trend, pretty much anything that gives us better confidence in the setup. Google "Forex Confluence" if you are not sure what I am talking about.

When I have found a proper setup I set an alarm just above the sweetzone so that I don't have to watch the pair every minute.

That's about it, good luck

--- 帖子 #183 ---
Edit: The way we want to trade the Wolfe Wave here is that the trade is not valid until we hit the Sweet zone. Just the Wolfe Wave is valid as long as the D breaks outside of the X-B trendline.

A WW is not really valid until we hit the sweet zone. If this zone is hit, it can only invalidate by moving too far from the wave (channel), hitting the stoploss (This means that it was more of a breakout than a fakeout).

If you mean before the sweetzone is hit, anything that invalidates the structure is invalidating the wave, for instance if price takes too long from wave A to B, or from C to D (meaning that there is no symmetry in the AB=CD pattern), if price is generally whipsawing so no clear wave can be seen (remember to not force the setups) or if it breaks any of the trendlines (an example is in the picture below.)

Take care!

--- 帖子 #188 ---
Any pair and any time frame from 5 minutes to weekly.

Every day I start fresh. The only charts I leave up from the previous day are those that are still valid Wolfe waves that are still developing in the D leg.

I start with the majors and work my way through the list. A quick glance at the higher time frames and on down through the lower time frames. Since I do this every day I usually can skip many of the higher time frames because I already know there isn't any potential set up.

Generally speaking throughout the day you will be looking for hourly, 30 minute, 15 minute, and 5 minute set ups. The 4H and up set ups take so much longer you just need to map it once and monitor t for days or possibly weeks.

A good exercise is to pull up any pair and scroll thru a lower time frame as far back as you can and look for WWs and map them out. Just to see where the reversal happened and what the final result was.

Feel free to post any set ups you think are valid and we would be happy to check them out for you.

Cheers

--- 帖子 #232 ---
All we are doing is taking partial profits and moving SL to BE for the rest of the positions. Over time averaging in trades that make the target line the risk reward is much higher than 1:1

TP strategy and RR scenarios vary from trader to trader depending on your risk profile, acct size, etc etc

In that Kiwi trade we take 20 pips on 1/3 to 1/2 of our position. If we didn't, we incur the full loss of all positions as the trade reversed and moved below our initial SLs.

If finding stress free scalp systems that made 30 pips easy a day then we'd all be able to start with a 2k acct and be millionaires in a couple of years

But hey, you have to do what works for you

--- 帖子 #233 ---
Perfect! I like your SL and target too.

Just a thought. The AB=CD completion is about 5 pips short of the 161FIB. Higher time frames especially, I would break my total risk amount up and scale in with 3 positions starting at the 141FIB and ending at the 161FIB, kind of like dollar cost averaging. There is about 20 pips between those two levels so every 6 or 7 pips another position. Gives you a better total buy in price and lessens your risk. The down side is price may reverse before the 161FIB and your total position would be smaller. If the trade ended up a winner, then you'd make less

68 KB

880 downloads

Here is a little more in depth explanation of each element. Starts on page 32
http://www.forexmt4.com/_MT4_Systems...mics/TDI_1.pdf

For the TDI anglelator on the bottom right, it basically tells you the trend for each tine frame as well as the RSI conditions and a little bit more. I suggest you take a look at the inputs, it is somewhat self explanatory. For example, why the different colors for each number. It relates to how oversold or overbought price is on that particular time frame. Just scroll through the inputs and it will become clearer.

Hope that helps

--- 帖子 #272 ---
Not sure what your point is, maybe just showing a failed Wolfe wave?

Anyways, we can learn a lot by looking at failed WWs. For instance on this particular WW note:

1) The AB=CD completion level is 13 pips above the previous 2 month high, so taking this trade is potentially trading against a significant breakout level.

2) After the ABCD level was barely hit, if you look at the lower time frame, price initially bounced back down, as it so often does, to about 17 pips in the green. That's why I like to take at least 1/3 of my position off the table in profit and move the SLs to BE for the remaining 2/3's. Gives you a guaranteed small win with the potential for a home run. Otherwise, as was the case here, price reversed back up and blew out the original SLs and you incur the full value loss of the initial trade.

3) From a fundamental perspective, a different animal altogether, commodity prices, especially oil, have been selling off recently so going against that trend (i.e. shorting UCAD) is risky business

--- 帖子 #278 ---
I don't really expect this to get filled but nonetheless I wanted to share it. Also, I will scale in a bit early as it is likely there will be major supply as we get into 140.46 area, if we even make it that far

This a really good example of trying to short into the major resistance instead of trying to short after a break of major resistance.

GBP/JPY 15MIN CWW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

I stripped the same chart of everything but the AB=CD completion line and zoomed out on the hourly to show what I meant in my recent posts about major resistance. If the AB=CD completion line is above the major resistance and we are trying to short, then we are really playing with fire. Instead our AB=CD is exactly THE major resistance, so I am scaling in bit early. Also, we know where our SL will be. --- 帖子 #293 ---
Interesting way of thinking about it! Another way, without having to draw lines is to visualise a stairs type pattern.  These patterns generally occur after the strong phase of a trend; when a 'broad channel' has established - it will all depend on your time frame as to what 'broad' means.  At any rate, it would be a weaker stage of a trend.  So for a weak  bull trend / broad bull channel after every high, the bears are shorting and able to make money by taking the market back down below the prior major high.  As the bulls get weaker and the bears get stronger, the pullbacks get deeper and that is the harbinger of a bear move as eventually the bulls will run out of steam.  So I see that as the driver for the change in trend.  The Wolffe wave pattern, for me, is interesting, but I don't actually trade it - it's fun to find the patterns though! The other factors (bull / bear pressure) are what I feel are more important to get a grasp of.

--- 帖子 #299 ---
Hope everyone had a nice weekend.

Just some thoughts going forward:

1) Patience - It may be cliche, but let the trade come to you. Considering all of the pairs, not to mention all of the smaller time frames, we could easily find 100 WWs in a week. BUT, we only need a couple of good trades a week to make consistent pips.

2) Dangerous trades - Big news, small time frames, low liquidity. We just have to pass on these WWs

3) Filters - When we were kids we knew the guy smoking the non filter Camel cigarette was a rebel. Why? Because we knew it was more dangerous to his health. Same in trading. If we don't have confluence with filters, then we don't have the necessary edge.

Speaking of filters, I spent my extra time this weekend going over about 100 completed WWs. I slapped a pitchfork on the last swing up to the D leg and found this to have great potential as another filter for entry. Especially for steep waves and higher time frames where entry can be difficult. Coupled with our other filters, this could be very powerful.

Cherry picked of course but just to show the idea:

I actually tend to manually manage the trades. I only set the TPs around the standard 2:1 ratio so I don't miss any major spikes when I am away from the screen for longer periods of time (of course I can manage from my phone too but have been really busy lately)

For smaller time frames like this trade, if the trade moves to 1:1 like 15 pips or so, I will take profit on a few positions and let the other 2 run with trailing stop or just move SL to BE. I am definitely conservative on my TPs as a rule. Actually trying to train myself to let the winners run, one of my many weaknesses. Hi Expo, I was having a look at your setup and I have identified something that may be worth watching out for, but I am no expert - just learning.

Looking at the higher time frame charts there are various spikes and channels in operation and one such channel started on the 10th.  A retrace to the start of that channel would see a move to the higher rectangle shown on the inserted chart.  Apologies for all of the other dotted levels, but I have many S&R levels on my H1 charts.  The move between 6 and 8am this morning was quite strong (and was also a move from the bottom of a 15min channel to the top) and broke above a prior swing high / pivot at around 11498 and there is still a gap, which could be a measuring gap.  The leg leading up to that was 11498-11454=44 points so if that measuring gap stays open (or if there is obvious future support created by that gap), projecting up 44 points from 11498 would give a target of 11542 which is in the region of the channel retrace I referred to earlier.  Just my 2 penny worth and something to watch if your Wolfe Wave move doesn't get going.  I'm not saying it won't, but just something to bear in mind.

--- 帖子 #345 ---
In my opinion, you did not miss this setup as this is not a valid one.

Notice how AB is not equal to CD. For a good wolfe wave to complete, CD has to be equal or bigger/stronger than AB. Also, the perfect one is to enter somewhere when BD touched or price "pierced" through BD.

The second leg in this example is clearly shorter than AB.

Someone correct me if i am wrong. At least that's my definition of a good harmonic wolfe wave pattern. Still learning here also.

--- 帖子 #347 ---
Hard to say without having taken Bill Wolfe's course. In all of the free online resources that I looked at, I never saw any mention of it as a necessary element to entry. The charts I saw just said that price more often than not pierces into the sweet zone. The AB=CD was just something that I thought would act as another layer of confluence, especially since the sweet zone on higher time frames can be 100-300 pips. This was my main question as I tried to learn on my own. Where exactly do you enter inside the sweet zone?

As we have discussed a few times here already, other filters are surely needed for confluence and conformation. Right now I am looking at pitchforks, especially for flatter waves. Also, I think that Gann angles could be a very powerful tool in conjunction with WWs. I am trying to find a good free online study guide to learn more about Gann angles and fans. Creativity is only limited by our preconceptions of how it supposed to be done.

That's why wanted this thread to be learning journey for pros and newbies alike. Surely, anyone at anytime could come up with a brilliant new way of thinking. So far I am very pleased and encouraged by all of participation here.

The old saying, "United we stand, divided we fall" is very appropriate here at FF. I see way to many threads where ego trumps ego where people are too busy tearing each other down. The purpose here is to lift each other up.

--- 帖子 #369 ---
Hi Parviz, sorry been super busy all day just sat down to look at some charts and read new posts.

Yes, I think WWs in many instances are part of larger harmonic structures. And yes I have studied many harmonic structures over the years. I just like the simplicity of the WW and so I decided to focus on this one simple structure. I decided to try and be really good at one thing instead of being mediocre at many things.

I never got around to putting up a diagram for the AWW and PWW because the intent was to focus on the classic WW first. The anti wave was just something I noticed when studying 1000s of charts. I just gave it that generic name. I'm not sure but I believe Bill Wolfe traded parallel waves. I haven't taken his course so can't say for sure. However, I have seen others traders talk about it in other threads.

Here is an example of the AWW and PPW that I had saved on my computer. Not much different than the classic WW

AWW >> only difference is that line XB and AC are diverging, not converging, and because of this, the sweet zone is rarely penetrated as much as it is in the CWW. The AB=CD completion level tends to take place at the 113 or 127 FIB.

PWW >> only difference is that line XB is horizontal

When I get time I will try to update the first post with a diagram for each. Hope this helps for now.

I think all of those levels are useful in a given situation. For me, the wave angle has a lot to do with it. --- 帖子 #388 ---
Interesting situation and one that comes up quite often on bigger time frames.

My NZD/CHF 30MIN bullish PWW trade is still active, however, a bearish CWW developed on the 15MIN time frame. What to do? If it were at or near the target line or TP area then it would be a no brainer. End the trade manually and take the profits.

But in this case, my original trade is kind of still in its infancy. Also, if the smaller bearish wave were to complete to the target line, it still wouldn't hit the SL for the original trade. So, I will let the trade run its course for now.

All in all, I think this scenario is a good illustration and something that WW traders should always be watching out for. Waves are constantly in motion. They should be respected and monitored with due diligence.

--- 帖子 #410 ---
Wrapping up a very good week. Looking forward to clearing the charts and getting a fresh look for next week. I find Friday is a good time for reflection; to think about some errors we have made and how we will inject a new positive way of thinking and doing for the week ahead.

Less is often more

If you are struggling or on a string of losers, trade less. When we are looking for something, it's human nature to sometimes see something that really isn't there. The nature of this strategy is to find and trade Wolfe waves and I think sometimes it's natural to force price into the pattern we want to see. Price does what it does. It's our job to make sure price action fits the Wolfe wave parameters with the best possible structure.

A shiny car with a crappy engine isn't going to cut it in the long run. The old adage, "you can put lipstick on a pig, but it's still a pig" is very true here as well. We can draw lines and make all kinds of fancy diagrams and doll up our charts in every imaginable way, but if the nuts and bolts of our wave structure are faulty, then the chance for success is limited.

Demand quality from yourself and from your Wolfe waves. Always quality over quantity. There are 100+ valid waves each week, but you only need 2 or 3 to make your account grow consistently and significantly.

Confluence is king. Beware if it's not there.

Have a great weekend everyone and thanks for all of the posts this week. I am really pleased with how much work we have all done so far.

--- 帖子 #411 ---
This thread is really interesting

Timing, for me, could not be better as I'm investigating a kind of wave recently which allows the market to balance itself by causing some pain to the crowd.

The wolfe wave is really similar to this.

Do you ever thought about why they appear and tend to work more often than not?

Of course, many know that the market follows harmonics but there's also a big psychological component to it.

In my opinion, the market is designed to allow only a few to succeed and as soon as the crowd moves out of balance to a favored direction (short/long) the market has to rebalance itself in the interest of the few successful and smart traders.

So a wolfe wave is in essence a confirmed trend segment and we all know the story about HH HL (uptrend) - LL LH (downtrend) and what is written in the many trading books about how to trade a trend. Now, Bill Wolfe was genius to notice this and he even called it market balance when price moves from the sweet zone to the target EPA line which involves a break of structure in opposite direction with a wash out (stop hunt).

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Since the market is fractal in its nature, it makes sense to check the HTF waves and cycles in progress to make sure to not go against them.

Bill Wolfe wrote in his book that if price misses the EPA line often then he suggests to change the time frame because the dominant wave is probably on a different time frame:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Thanks Expo33 for the great and absolutely clear explanations and examples.

Learning about the sweet zone and your addition of using harmonics for confluence is a real insight.

Also nice results too, keep going

Hello Niaz, welcome to forex factory.

Thanks for using the template and for clearly marking everything out. It helps me a lot as my eyes are very sensitive.

I never want to dissuade someone from taking or not taking a trade as I certainly don't have all the answers but there are a couple of things I see with this trade that may present a problem.

First off, when I mapped this out it shows that XB is actually a bit less than parallel, so structurally this wave isn't technically valid. Not a deal breaker but certainly something to be aware of.

More importantly, there is a subsequent new wave developing here. Notice right now price is at a minor resistance, and then notice that the major resistance falls exactly where this new wave completes at the AB=CD level. I tried to make it clear on the chart. Also interesting is the spot where price reversed on your initial wave, exactly at point C of the new wave. Probably not a coincidence.

CAD/JPY DAILY CWW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

I'll preface this next chart by saying I am in my infancy in studying Gann angles. One thing I do know is they supposedly work better on higher time frames. Gann angles are unique in that they map out price AND time. I put a Gann angle on our chart and it seems to paint an interesting picture.

Gann theory says that when price breaks through one angle it is likely to continue to the next angle. In our scenario the 1x1 (45 degree) angle has been broken and price is heading towards the 1x2 angle. Interesting to note on our new wave that the 1x3 Gann angle crosses very near the ETA (Estimated Time of Arrival), which just happens to be near the 200FIB AND AB=CD completion level. Is price heading down to that point of confluence? I don't know but if it breaks through the 1x2 Gann angle, it could be.

Here is the same chart as above but with the Gann angles shown

CAD/JPY DAILY CWW WITH GANN ANGLES
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Anyways ,that's my analysis for the chart you posted. I hope it helps in some way. Thanks again for posting and good trading to you. Please feel free to post any charts that you have questions about or anything else you want to share with us.

Regards,

-Kurt

--- 帖子 #433 ---
Consider this a failed example? Or stoploss not wide enough?

Edit: I just found out that if the start of C leg is robust or very volatile, it's usually bad for the CD leg or it may extend longer

CD LEG VARIATIONS

These CD leg phenomena can be described in four ways:

1.

If after point C has occurred a gap exists in the direction of point D,

this usually indicates that the CD leg will be much greater than the AB

leg—1.272, 1.618, or more.

2.

A wide range bar (twice normal size) at point C is another indication

that the CD leg could become extended.

3.

Ideally, AB

=

CD moves are symmetrical in price and time. For exam-

ple, if the AB leg is six bars up, then the CD leg will be six bars up.

A lot of different view points I'm sure.

1) Original bounce lower from AB=CD = 1.4032 was about 15 pips, so there would have been the opportunity to move SL to BE.

2) Very volatile pair. In hindsight a 30 SL would have covered it. That's not really that big of a SL considering a minimum move back to the X level was about 60 pips. Smaller position sizes needed for sure.

3) Big 2 candle D leg power move up automatically makes the candle symmetry very bad so a warning signal right from the start. Zooming out to the hourly and waiting for a TDI cross takes away the uncertainty of that whole volatile sweet zone.

4) Plenty of other opportunities. I think just the act of passing is a very good mental exercise in patience and is a building block to becoming a ninja type Wolfe wave stalker!

With due diligence we can always attempt to find a solution to our problem: Where do we enter the trade?

--- 帖子 #453 ---
I could also contribute some thoughts to this interesting thread (once again thanks to Expo for initiating). I would echo the thoughts of LDFX in that it would be extremely difficult to code this sort of thing and, more importantly, that confluence is the key. The attached chart should help to explain the confluence effect and why the market turned where it did on Friday afternoon. There is no substitute for hard work and looking for likely Support and Resistance including, but not limited to, prior highs and lows, trend and channel lines, signal bar highs and lows, measured move targets, previous day OHLC etc. A Wolfe Wave is a reversal pattern and will only ever take place at support or resistance so trying to identify these areas is the key. So what can we identify from the H4 chart attached?

1) A channel line from 8 Dec through Feb 2 and extended to the right (I tend to think that tails on top / bottom of bars represent slight over-extension when testing a level so I look for a likely place for the line to pass through in real time. Here, we have the benefit of hindsight).

2) Sunday 5th Feb produced a bear signal bar (circled) whose low had not yet been tested and was , therefore, a magnet.

3) Late Feb into early March produced a trading range and double bottom bull flag pattern which afforded a measured move target as shown by the red bars so was another magnet.

4) The yellow bars represent a leg 1 = leg 2 measured move. It is possible to get a better approximation than the move shown by looking at where the likely start and end of the first leg really were. For instance, I would surmise that the first leg started with a test of the March 3 signal bar high and finished on the channel line just under the yellow bar at around 10700, but again that is easy to say with the benefit of hindsight - at any rate, another magnet was in the same general area.

So we have 4 resistance points clustered in the same area and that confluence of resistance led to a reversal and maybe the start of the Wolfe Wave playing out.

An obvious downside target where support may kick in is the signal bar high on Mar 15th @ around 10640.

--- 帖子 #466 ---
Hi, I was giving this some thought over the weekend and I don't think that it is entirely true that it is purely a countertrend pattern.  I suppose it depends on one's perspective.  For instance, suppose we have a broad bull channel on, say, the H4 timeframe where price has come down to touch the trend line.  Let's take a textbook TR / channel scenario where we are looking at a nice two legs up from the bottom to the top of the channel.  The pullback in between the legs could very well have the stair-stepping pattern on a lower timeframe (say 15min) indicative of a Wolfe Wave setup on that timefreame, but to a price action trader it is merely a flag where a bull breakout towards the top of the H4 channel is expected.  Therefore, although the Wolf Wave is reversing the smaller 15min trend, the trade is in the direction of the H4 trend and therefore a continuation setup and higher probability.

Or am I stating the bleeding obvious?!

--- 帖子 #471 ---
I think you have completely missed the point of what I am saying.

If it was not clear, then my apologies.  The way many traders enter trends is by waiting for a pullback - agreed?  By definition, a pullback is a smaller trend in the opposite direction so entering the main trend again is trading counter and against the momentum of the pullback. Obviously the pullback has to be weak in relation to the trend.   So, a higher probability way to trade the Wolfe Wave pattern is to identify the setup on a lower time frame during a pullback in an obvious higher time frame trend.  Makes perfect sense to me, but then again, I accept that my beliefs about the market may not be useful to others.  You pay your money and take your choice.

--- 帖子 #472 ---
Ok now I see what you are trying to trade. It's not a classic Wolfe wave because line XB and AC don't converge. Technically it fits my made up definition of an Anti wave because those two lines are diverging. Unfortunately the structure and symmetry are really not very good

--- 帖子 #473 ---
hi dude,

I totally got your point, for me any pull back is a counter trend entry, the wolfe wave being one of the most needed trend in order to unfold, x abcd needs time and space aka a trend.

A stop order above the high would be a trend continuation entry, there is of course trend continuation patterns but that are taken in counter trend.

To make it simple, when price makes lower low and you buy, it is a counter trend entry, if price makes higher high and you buy it is a trend continuation entry.

--- 帖子 #474 ---
Hey,

Fair enough.  The way you view the market is no doubt useful to you and that's great.  For me there are many ways to view situations.  For example, as a trend trader you would bet on most attempts to reverse the trend being unsuccessful.  Therefore buying on a limit order below prior bars in a bull trend can be a prudent thing to do. One would be betting on continuation of the trend, but if the prior bar was a bear bar (and therefore a bear trend on some lower timeframe) by your definition it would be a purely counter trend trade.  I guess it's all a matter of perspective.

--- 帖子 #477 ---
Mate, we are talking at cross-purposes.

Like I said, it's all about perspective and timeframe.  What I am suggesting is using the lower time frame Wolfe Wave set up to enter the larger trend which can be expected to continue (since most reversal attempts fail).  It is perfectly feasible, in a bull trend on one timeframe to have a bear bar, which when dissected on some lower time frame, could contain a Wolf Wave setup. Entering on a limit below that higher time frame bear bar is identical to trading the Wolf Wave on the lower timeframe.  So yes, I totally agree that it is counter trend to the lower time frame trend - although it is debatable whether it would really be a trend as a Wolf Wave setup (generally) has many overlapping bars and is really an expanding trading range.

It is a different kettle of fish entirely if the Wolfe Wave setup takes the market below a  prior MAJOR low (ie a low after which the market had a strong breakout to give a new high) on the chart on which you are looking to enter the trend.  Minor lows get taken out all of the time during two / three / x legged pullbacks and are of no consequence

What I am not talking about here is the more classical reversal Wolfe Wave at the top or bottom of a trend.  In these cases I agree that most set ups will fail because that is the nature of reversals.

The idea is to add value to this thread and try to come up with ways to improve the Wolfe Wave strategy for those who actually trade it.  By thinking about it from a pure price action point of view, using different timeframes can help to gain perspective.

All the best.

When a wolfe wafe is unfolding you do take entry on a lower low that is the 3rd low of the wolf wave pattern, if that is not a counter trend...

--- 帖子 #504 ---
This is the new version, it detect WW when the following conditions are true :

if(

Low[Wolf[1]]<High[Wolf[2]] &&

Low[Wolf[3]]<Low[Wolf[1]] &&

Low[Wolf[3]]<High[Wolf[4]] &&

High[Wolf[4]]>Low[Wolf[1]] &&

Low[Wolf[5]]<=Low[Wolf[3]]

)

{

WolfWave="Buy";

}

//---------------------

if

(

High[Wolf[1]]>Low[Wolf[2]] &&

High[Wolf[3]]>High[Wolf[1]] &&

High[Wolf[3]]>Low[Wolf[4]] &&

Low[Wolf[4]]<High[Wolf[1]] &&

High[Wolf[5]]>=High[Wolf[3]]

)

{

WolfWave="Sell";

}

And it also print all five standard fibo relations of harmonic patterns and now the position of text can be set .

Any suggestions, ideas, reporting bugs found..., are most welcome and appreciated.

--- 帖子 #514 ---
Hi all:

If you read the wolfe book on finding the necessary points that form WW wave you notice he suggest to find them in order of 2,3,1,4 and finally 5,

Let me give you another idea which i believe may help novices like me to find any harmonics pattern including WW .

1)Find any combination of waves that form a (W) or (M) shape .

2) Just put your B(3) point in the center of (W) oR (M).

3) on The opposite side of the B(3) there are 2 point on right and left of the B(3) name them A(2) and C(4) respectively.

4) Now the end of the right leg is X(1) point and that of the left one is D(5) .

5)Connect with two Trend Line point X(1) to B(3) and point A(2) to C(4) respectively.

6) Now You have the pattern , if the two Trend Line converge You Have the setting for WW ready and should wait for completion of D(5)point.

7) Otherwise compare it to the other harmonic patterns using the cheat sheets and 5 fibo relations.

I hope this will help many who are still confused about labelling the points and legs .

--- 帖子 #554 ---
Just tried to fix bugs and better detection of CWW...

pictures above ,show it at work.

Logic for detection changed as follow :

if(

Low[Wolf[1]]<High[Wolf[2]] &&

Low[Wolf[3]]<High[Wolf[4]] &&

Low[Wolf[3]]<Low[Wolf[1]] &&

High[Wolf[4]]<High[Wolf[2]]&&

((ObjectGetValueByShift(Title+"Line-1-3",Wolf[5])>=Low[Wolf[5]]) && xa>bc)

)

{

WolfWave="Buy";

}

else if

(

High[Wolf[1]]>Low[Wolf[2]] &&

High[Wolf[3]]>Low[Wolf[4]] &&

High[Wolf[3]]>High[Wolf[1]] &&

Low[Wolf[4]]>Low[Wolf[2]] &&

((ObjectGetValueByShift(Title+"Line-1-3",Wolf[5])>=Low[Wolf[5]]) && xa>bc )

)

{

WolfWave="Sell";

}

else

{

WolfWave="None";

}

Keeps getting better and better!!

Thinking about what has to happen to set up an alert. We can think of the current Price as a moving Point D, which will eventually become fixed or fail.

So in order to anticipate a successful D, we could look for the case where Price has moved say 90 % of the target given by the length of AB in pips.

so when   C - Price >90% of A-B, send alert ......" bullish CWW developing"

and when Price - C > 90% of B -A send alert..... "bearish CWW developing"

Which means price is approaching the sweet zone and we can start to look for a possible trade. I suggest the 90% level as an arbitrary guess, might have to be less, would likely depend on the time frame, shorter time frames might require a different % than longer ones, no idea how to figure that out, might just take experience.

anyway thanks for all of your hard work and let  me know if this  makes sense to  you.

--- 帖子 #582 ---
Folks,

Perfect patterns are hard to come by.  In general with trading, close is close enough.  There are many occasions in Bill Wolfe's book where he fudges the start point of the pattern to fit by placing it horizontal to point 3 when it actually has no business being there.  Maybe it was a case of curve-fitting after the event to show trades that work.  To be honest, there are loads of set ups every day that fail so it is a matter of trying to read the chart.  I would suggest looking at whatever setup you find and analysing it objectively.  Can you see Support or resistance around the area you think the market may reverse (and by the way, apart from using fib retracement / extension tools for a leg 1=leg 2 projection, using Fibs are next to useless.  50% is pretty much the only retracement that has any statistical significance and there are very sound mathematical reasons for that!).  The line that the Wolfe Wave generates to give a projected price target is useful in that you can use it to look for obvious support or resistance around that price.  Obviously, when looking to see if a Wolfe Wave is worth trading, it is extremely worthwhile looking to see if there are any adverse magnets that will scupper your trade, if you are in the habit of catching falling knives ( and whatever the opposite may be); if the market is heading somewhere it is usually more obvious on the higher time frame charts (H1, H4).

I hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #585 ---
Hi Parviz,

OK the mathematical rationale for a 50% retracement is very simple, but I shall go into a little more detail.

Risk, reward and PROBABILITY.

In order for a trade to make mathematical sense the following must be true:

P(Success)*Reward - P(Failure)*Risk > 0

Probability is the concept that never gets mentioned when traders talk about a trade.  In general they only say 'it's got great risk-reward' and maybe they are right, but only if the probabilities stack up.  With any trade, someone (an institution) has to take the other side of it.  They are not going to take the other side of your trade if they have a tiny probability of winning, and you trade could be buy OR sell.  Therefore, we have to assume that trading survives in a constant fog of probability between say 40 and 60% ie. If you are confident something will happen, then you may have a 60% chance of it occurring.  Traders always want Low risk, High probability, massive reward trades.  They cannot exist! There are fleeting moments throughout the day when probability may approach 70-80% (I wish I could spot them in time!) but the market quickly moves to close this down and probability once again hovers somewhere around the 50% mark ie 50% probability of moving x ticks before an x tick stop is hit.

So, lets take a bull case.  The market has had a strong bull leg and you are impressed with it; impressed enough to think you want to buy a pullback.  The implication is that you feel that the market may be trending and you want to get in on the move.  Trending would then imply that you think the market will make a higher high, at least by a small amount.  As you think the market is trending and the market tends to keep doing what it has been doing then we can surmise that we have a 60% probability of making a new high.  A 50% pullback on the move means that you are midway between where the market is telling you that you need your stop and the high of the move.  Therefore it is the point where Risk (R) = Reward (R). So taking probability into account P(success = 0.6)*R - P(Failure = 0.4)*R = 0.2R > 0 so it is mathematically logical to take the trade or as Al Brooks would say 'it has a positive traders' equation'.  If we ignore the concept of probability then we can just say that a 50% pullback is the point at which our potential reward is equal to our risk.

Quite long-winded, but I hope that explains it thoroughly.

Here are a few charts which will help to explain a Wolfe Wave which happens to be part of a trading idea.

The first chart is a H1 of EURUSD.  We can see the trend line from the 9th was broken on the 29th.  We would usually expect a test of the trend extreme after a decent break of the trend line.  We got the decent break of the trend line and there has been a reasonable tight bear channel from the trend extreme. At the moment it looks like support has been found at a prior signal bar high (circled) and also on another channel line dating back to the 22nd.  This channel line also has the 1,3 and maybe the 5 point on it.  The target line for the wave I am talking about is drawn in thick red.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

However, we don;t know if the market will reverse back up so I now want to identify a reversal on a lower time frame chart such as the 5min.  As we can see, there is another Wolfe Wave possibility on this lower time frame.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

At the moment, although we can see a clear channel line across three lows, the last leg down was far too strong to think about going long.  I would want to see a stronger break of the steep trend line followed by an attempt at bear trend resumption.  I would be looking for a failure of the bear trend resumption at a support level, such as a signal bar high and maybe even a  wedge bottom.  I would then want a decent bull signal bar after the bulls have shown decent strength and that they may have the ability to take control over the market.

--- 帖子 #601 ---
Been trading WWs for years.  The secret is that the 'X' must be a new high or low. You can't have an X in mid price obscurity.  WWs exist at the bottom and tops of moves and the best ones stand out -you shouldn't need an Indy to spot them!

The target price should, IMHO (and Linda Rache's) be the intersection of the line connecting points 1 & 4 of the wave where this meets the vertical point where the X-B; A-C line convergence joins.

Point 3 must be higher than 1 when looking at WW short and vice versa.  The lines must converge to give the 'wedge' pattern

Bill Wolfe prints many patterns in his book and many of them are not the perfect pattern with the leg1= leg2 and some of the 3-4-5 waves are extremely small (noise apparently) compared to the prior 1-2-3 wave. Good luck to all of you traders out there!

--- 帖子 #630 ---
Hi L.m,

Thank you for your feedback.  No offence has been taken.

Just to clarify a couple of points.....I do look at Wolfe Waves and use them to look for reversal trades and I use a Fib tool sometimes to look for Leg 1 =Leg 2 moves. I have posted some charts with the Fib levels on them purely for seeing where a leg 1 = leg 2 would be.  The reason I have no real time for Fibs is that the market movement is basically controlled by computers. If more computers / money think that resistance is at point A than point B then the market will turn at Point A.  This is purely my opinion, but I very much doubt whether the computers have 'look for a 161% Fib extension and place a trade' algorithm.  Maybe I am wrong.  If someone could explain a mathematical rationale for Fibs working in the market  and back it up with some decent evidence then I am willing to be convinced otherwise.  Until then I will just use good old support and resistance. Adam Grimes has done quite a bit of statistical analysis on Fib levels and he could find no evidence for Fibs working.

The main reason I was frustrated is that some of my charts are not perfect examples of Wolfe Waves, but they are a type of Wolfe Wave as I understand it from reading Bill Wolfe's book.  The charts below are taken directly from the Wolfe book.  I have conceded that some of my charts are not brilliant examples in terms of symmetry, but in terms of looking for reversals they are not too dissimilar to those posted below. So I have not sought to mislead anyone and I do genuinely seek to help.  When I was laughed at for a trade not going as hoped and being breakeven rather than a winner, I decided that there was no point posting any more when there is childish behavior like that directed at me.  I am not prepared to tolerate that and have better things to do with my time.  Once again, thank you for your feedback and all the best.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #631 ---
Agree - we are not trying to 'berate' anyone; just point people in the right direction. You need to learn this stuff over years. See attached example for clarity.

In short, don't look and try to curve-fit patterns to charts where WW or any price action doesn't exist!

Look for a rising / falling wedge. Then apply the basic WW 'rules'. Draw your lines. 3 and 5 must be higher than 1. 4 must be higher than 2. The wedge lines MUST converge in the future. Await price action at point 5 before selling. Use support levels or ATR targets to set limit orders, or whatever MM you use. Simples.

See attached example on USDCHF that I traded and tweeted about.

--- 帖子 #663 ---
Hi sir:

1)If the indicator find any pattern, then it sets a find flag , make an alert, and stop searching, so if you already have a pattern found and drawn on your chart, its not going to do it again.

2) With so many rules that need to be true for the curve to be acceptable as a valid CWW, it may take a while before it forms if ever.

3) Don't forget that in a time frame while ,one setting (ExtDepth of 6), may not find any, others(ExtDepth of 3 or 12) may.

4) As i said before it is best when used as a scanning tool, put it on a pair , go through different TF , and if you find an interesting and valid CWW then make a note and follow it closely.

By the way check the input for setting and set alert to true, if not done before, and if it find any it is going to give you repeated alarm on every new Bar of that TF,so if it is on M15 it will alert every 15 minute.

--- 帖子 #672 ---
Thanks for your indi, it's very useful to quickly scroll the pairs and TF. I think the patterns need to be checked before opening any trade. Since it's based on zigzag it depends by its settings whether the pattern is correct or not.

According to Wolfe, between X(1) and B(3) there can't be another swing low (swing high for rising patterns) so the one in your picture is not a real WW pattern. I've seen others and it was something I wanted to point out, sorry to be late.

I don't think it's possible to solve this issue, just need to check the patterns. But there's a second point I would like to talk about and take the occasion since Expo is here again (welcome back Expo) because I would like to know what he thinks about it. Point X(1) according to the original rules should be between B(3) and C(4) and to me it's an important rule (not included but easy to add in your indi) because if point C(4) fails to clearly break point X(1) it means the trend is strong and the reverse may take longer before to begin.

Hi All:

Somebody before has asked me about wether my indicator is repainting or not? and i said not.

Now Let me elaborate more on this issue technically :

When the indicator find and draw a valid, either a potential or a completed CWW, then as i said it set a found flag and stop repainting it, but the program is still running and on formation of every new ZigZag high or low ,it look to see if it is a new valid one according to the definition of CWW,  and if it does then it will repaint again.

I hope this explanation would be of help regarding this important question.

--- 帖子 #706 ---
Hi everybody:

Let me confess that i did not know anything about the CWW, before entering and reading this forum, a generous and excellent work of Expo,.

Now after a deep dive into the definition and its characteristics and coding an indicator for it, I want to define what a CWW is in my humble opinion and as I understand it:
1) CWW is a variant (mutant) form of Elliot's wave, which has been very well defined by the great job of Mr Wolfe, and works as good as it's decent father.

2) It start one extremum of price moves later than Elliot's waves, (X point of it is indeed 1st point of the Elliot's).So a bullish Elliot's wave is a bearish Wolfe wave (look at the superimposed picture of my last post).

3) While in Elliot's Wave, all believe that the best point to enter the market is at the beginning of the formation of 3rd wave(the impulsive 3rd wave), wolfe wave trader are advised to enter the market on the completion of the D(5) point, which is indeed, upon completion of the 5th wave and beginning of the retracement Waves of Elliot's (at the beginning of its ABC wave formation).

4) So, while trades of Elliot's wave follower start "with the trend" at the completion of 2nd point, wolfe's trader wait till trend is finished and its retracement start("Anti_trend trading", beginning at its well defined, best selected point of it ,the "Sweet Zone").

I am looking forward for any comments that teach me, if i am wrong in any parts, or overlooked any details.

Dear expo please mentor me, if i am wrong.

--- 帖子 #707 ---
As I stated previously, not always, but CWWs are often the end points of larger harmonic structures, including Eliiot waves.

However, I can't comment on Elliot waves specifically as I haven't really studied them in depth. I think there have been some knowledgeable EW posters here that have made some very good points on this subject.

--- 帖子 #766 ---
Hi All, thank you for a great thread,

and hats off to Parvis for his coding.

I would like to share a few things that have dropped into place

while following the thread.

For me, they are very [VERY] significant.

First you would need to take a look at the attached pics.

They represent the Harmonic Elliott Wave [HEW] Impulse Wave Count,

in 5 waves [(i) to (v)].

To keep it simple, I have added the 1 to 5 basic Wolfe Wave Count.

Also, each and every Wave a and Wave c is a HEW 5 wave Impulse Wave.

Now, that's a lot of 5 wave HEW 5 wave Impulse Waves!

And, that's a lot of Wolfe Waves that end each HEW Impulse Wave.

Virtually an endless supply!

Not only that, the Wave b corrections also contain HEW 5 wave Impulse Waves.

They can be very complicated,

but we already know how complicated corrections can be!

The Wave ii's and iv's also contain 5 wave Impulse Waves.

Cheers, U2

--- 帖子 #768 ---
[

Hi Uturn:

Thank a lot for you kind complement.

I believe you are making a mistake, when you were naming the CWW counterpart of the HEW, i believe you must start counting one wave later, please refer to my post#704, to see what i mean.

in confirmation of what i said, consider also that for a CWW to be valid X(1) need to be between point B(3) , and C(4).

the third point that i want to mention is that as you said there are a lot of different level of CWW as HEW, and it depends on how you define the ExtDepth of the zigzag indicator ,which gives you larger or smaller high and lows and peak and lawn.

a valid CWW has a strict rules that as a reminder i write it again here for information of all:

Buy Wolf wave:

Low[X]<High[A] &&

Low[X]<High[C] &&

Low[b]<High[C] &&

Low[b]<Low[X] &&

High[C]<High[A]&&

(slope1_3<=slope2_4)&&

D(5) should touch or pass Line1_3&&

D(5) should not pass the boundary of 2nd sweet zone

And you can think , the same form of logic is there, for detection of a Sell Wolfe wave.

EDITED:

And the last point:
Wolfe waves are not impulsive wave of HEW, but indeed the retracement wave of it. And this is why CWW lags one wave later on HEW, as i mentioned earlier.

Hi All:

In this new version, i have added some new features, which i believe, would be very helpful.

1) Now you may put, fibo on any line segment of the wave as you wish, and clear it whenever you want, each of the button act as toggle . you may have two or more fibos at the same time.

2) The other one is "SAVE PATTERN" button, by clicking on it an image of the current pattern is saved on the chart, so that you may move between different TF, and compare it in with other TF pattern or if a new pattern comes in it is not gonna be lost.(if at any time you don't want to have it , go to the object list and remove the objects with time and date stamped in their name, or rerun your template).

--- 帖子 #786 ---
pls. help me on this zig zag thing....bro!

###########################

double ZigZag2[100];

double LastOne2[2];

int cc2=0;

int dd2=0;

void Zigzag2()

{

for(int Count=0;Count<=99;Count++)

{

if(cc2>1){break;}

ZigZag2[Count]=iCustom(NULL,0,"ZigZag",12,5,3,0,Count);

if (ZigZag2[Count]!=0)

{

LastOne2[cc2]=ZigZag2[Count];

cc2=cc2+1;

if (cc2==1) {dd2=Count+1;}

}

}

double ZigValue=LastOne2[0];

double ZigValue1=LastOne2[1];

checkCreateHorizontalLine(0, objectsName + "ZZHigh", 0, ZigValue, clrGray);

checkCreateHorizontalLine(0, objectsName + "ZZLow", 0, ZigValue1, clrGray);

}

######################################

Using above code i get last 2 swings value, but the value don't update themselfs....

any idea to change the code and get the latest 2 swings value?

--- 帖子 #788 ---
It is really coded in a very hard way, and does not have any comments, but anyhow try this if it would be of any help:

double ZigZag2[100];

double LastOne2[2];

int i=0;

double Temp=0;

for(int Count=0;Count<=99;Count++)

{

Temp=iCustom(NULL,0,"ZigZag",12,5,3,0,Count)

if(Temp != EMPTY_VALUE)

{

LastOne2[i]=Temp;

i++;

}

}

1)I should read its code to see how it would be possible.

2)Each item on the chart has a time and a price dimension, price axis scale change exponentially, so ten pip higher on higher places on chart is equal sometimes to 100 pips in some places lower on the same chart so with different price variation on different charts the location of the X,A,B,C,D text will change, so i decided to put it right were the price is and only shift the time value to the right, for location to be fixed, for all kind of price movement within the visible chart area.

I respectfully disagree.

On a daily chart we may be talking anywhere from 20-100 pips or more for 5-10%. Lower lows, higher highs was the original principle behind the WW. However, Bill Wolfe did show examples where the XB line was horizontal (the parallel WW which probably should be called the horizontal WW)

Point being, this may be a Pandora's box. Where does it end? Why not 12%, etc ,etc. Especially considering any new traders that may be starting their new WW journey. Just more confusion if they have perused the other free online resources related to WWs.

Maybe it's best for traders to just draw the wave manually if they want to stretch the parameters in this way.

Just my thoughts

--- 帖子 #806 ---
Hi Expo :

1) Find this part of the code near the end of program: else LabelPos = Low[ib]; , it has been repeated two times.

2) change both of them with this code : else LabelPos = NormalizeDouble(Low[ib]-0.5*iATR(NULL,0,10,ib),Digits);

3)Now compile it and use, problem solved.

4) you can change the position vertically, by modifying the 0.5 coefficient to other numbers, there are four of them 2 for High's and 2 for Low's.

--- 帖子 #808 ---
Hi :

Just i want to mention few thing about the charts that you are sharing.

1) I believe the way you count the waves is a problem, you mixes waves of different fractal levels in counting.

2) The HEW as far as i Know, usually moves in a channel, the first wave 1 , comes from a point outside the channel (point X) to form the first impulse wave #1 , then it retrace forms #2, after that another usually the largest wave #3 and so on to the fifth wave, the fifth wave, in 50% of the HEW, may not rich the upper channel line, and is referred to as The aborted fifth wave. reteracement of this wave is the beginning of corrective waves abc and/or even abcde. This is the wave which makes the third touch of price with trend line and will eventually break it.

3)some of the waves that you are counting are not as large as it should be, they are smaller waves of a lower fractals(Noises)

4) The best location to trade is at the beginning of #3 wave in HEW, which is a big challenge to locate so early in it formation, and resulted in most of my failures..., in contrast CWW best trade location is at the beginning of the corrective wave abc, after formation of D(5) point, which locating this one too, plays with your soul and money....

5) HEW suggest trading with the trend buy, in upward moving channel, while an up going CWW is called a SELL CWW wave and suggest to take a sell trade, after D(5) completion.

These are just my idea, no offense.

--- 帖子 #809 ---
Hi Parvis,

The Elliott Wave I follow is called Harmonic Elliott Wave.

It differs from Traditional Elliott Wave.

It simplifies the wave count, and clears up some of the ambiguities of Elliott Wave.

There are no failed fifth waves in HEW, or channel constraints.

Easiest way to understand it would be to watch the introduction video.
http://www.harmonic-ewave.com/

Cheers, U2
