--- 帖子 #872 ---
Hi Poruchik.

An "Anti Wolfe wave" has the same structure as the classic Wolfe wave except that it is divergent. For example, line XB and line AC are diverging instead of converging. It does NOT fit the definition of a classic Wolfe wave, hence the name "Anti" Wolfe wave.

I am going to remove the Anti WW from the first post and the thread as it's basically causing confusion. I should have never added it in the first place. Better we all just focus on the one classic structure as defined by Mr. Wolfe himself.

Hope that helps.

Cheers, -Kurt

--- 帖子 #893 ---
Hi Shuo and welcome to the thread.

I'll try to answer your questions the best that I can.

1) The indicator chooses potential/completed waves based on the zig zag "ext depth" setting. For instance, one setting might not show a valid wave while a different setting may show a valid wave. I suggest you put the indicator on a chart and change the "extdepth" to each different setting and see what happens. The indicator automatically chooses point D so that the length of segment AB = CD. This doesn't mean that the last leg (CD) will necessarily reach that point, it just shows you where the exact completion point would be if AB were to exactly equal CD. The indicator will give you point D as soon as the CD leg starts, in other words as soon as the zig zag determines point C.

Here is an example where price reversed 61 pips before the D point. Note how the indicator shows where the AB=CD point is even though the price never actually made it down that far.

NZD/CAD DAILY CWW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

2) Not necessarily. Where you set your order will depend on your personal filtering system. I like to scale in with multiple positions as prices moves into my sweet zone. This is where there is some subjectivity in how you enter. Many traders will wait for the price to reverse, maybe wait for the TDI to cross. I like to use the BC FIB extension, previous S/R, and Gann fans as my filters. I ook for a "zone" for entry not a static price.

3) Again, stop loss will depend on your own personal risk profile. I tend to put my stops below the next FIB extension level. Each trade varies and my stop loss may be dependent on factors that are only particular to that trade.

Hope this helps, any other questions I will try to answer as best I can.

Thanks for posting and best trading to you.

-Kurt

PS. Hopefully Parviz will correct me if I'm wrong. I'm also still learning the finer points of this indicator.

--- 帖子 #901 ---
Let me tell you an interesting point , get the reciprocal of any of the known fibonacci relations (.382,.5,.618,.707,.786,.886) and you get these secondary fibo relation numbers(2.618,2.0,1.618,1.41,1.27,1.13) and whenever you have point C retracement of the first set you expect to get to the amount of the 2nd set projection of Bc.......!!!

In simple math, we can say : the amount of projection of BC has inverse relationship with amount of C retracement.

And here I quote a part of a good book on harmonic trading by Scott M. Carney

Harmonic Trading Ratios
Primary Ratios:
(Directly derived from the Fibonacci Number Sequence)
0.618 = Primary Ratio
1.618 = Primary Projection
Primary Derived Ratios: 0.786 = Square root of the 0.618 ( ) 0.886 = Fourth root of 0.618 or Square root of the 0.786 ( 1.13 = Fourth root of 1.618 or

Square root of the 1.27 ( ) 1.27 = Square root of the 1.618 (
Complementary Derived Ratios:   0.382 = (1-0.618) or 0.6182 0.707 = Square root of 0.50 ( ) 1.41=Squarerootof2.0( ) 2.0 = (1+1) 2.24=Squarerootof5( ) 2.618 = 1.6182  3.14 = Pi (See later section The Importance of Pi (3.14) in Harmonic Trading) 3.618 = (1+2.618)

--- 帖子 #905 ---
This is another pragraph from the same book:

[
AB=CD Reciprocal Ratios
In the AB=CD pattern, the alignment of Fibonacci ratios within the structure usually manifests specific reciprocal relationships. The reciprocal ratio of the C point retracement of the AB leg usually indicates which BC projection is utilized to define the Potential Reversal Zone (PRZ). For instance, a 0.618 retracement at the C point typically will possess a 1.618 BC projection that converges closest with the completion of the AB=CD. This reciprocal relationship within the equivalent AB=CD pattern defines the best PRZ for this structure. The reciprocal ratios that complement the AB=CD structure are as follows:
C Point Retracement 0.382
0.50 0.618 0.707 0.786 0.886
BC Projection .24 or 2.618
2.0 1.618 1.41 1.27 1.13
The reciprocal ratios help define the completion of the pattern. However, the most important consideration to remember is that the BC projection should converge closely with the completion of the AB=CD.

when c retracement is .382 then projection is either 2.41 or 2.618(this is exactly copied from the book and there is, interestingly a printing error of .24 ,instead of 2.41)

EDITTED : OH sorry you are right my mistake it was indeed 2.24 and the first number was missed in printing the table.but here i found another source . Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #915 ---
The bigger wave always takes precedence over the smaller wave when taking a trade. If you look at post #915 you can see the stop loss for the bigger wave allows the trade to breath properly.

Smaller waves that develop inside bigger waves are used more for exit. For example, you trade a 4H bullish WW and half way to your target price a bearish WW develops on the hourly, maybe time to exit early.

2) There is a factor in input that you may select relative position for values, i have preset it to 10 , you may change it till it fits your taste.

3) You may select to show zigzag line and the values in input, if set to false it does not show either .

PS:By the way i am working on a new version which is going to automate every thing :

1) It look for all 6 Extdepth that you set in the input and draw every thing that can be find and draw them all.

2) for every depth it first look for possible Completed CWW, if can not find any, then it will look for the Potential ones.

3)After it has done that, then you may select which one of the patterns you like to keep and erase the others.

Indeed 70% of the program has been coded already, the reason that i am talking about it now is that, the code is ever growing bigger and bigger and when it is finished it would be really hard to change any part of it. Hello my friend,

I thinks there is only one thing need to be changed...

X must touch C, dont u think this rule is too strict?

Sometimes X just a few pips away from C, and that makes the signal invalid...

could u pls. add a range function for X and C based on ADR distance and TF.

EX.

mathabs(X-C)<35% ADR   XC touched = true; (for Period()=D1)   if ADR is 100pips, X-C<35pips =  singal valid

mathabs(X-C)<20% ADR   XC touched = true; (for Period()=H4)

mathabs(X-C)<10% ADR   XC touched = true; (for Period()=H1)

mathabs(X-C)<5% ADR   XC touched = true; (for Period()=M15)

--- 帖子 #958 ---
Here, code for ADR...

point=Point;

if( Digits==3 || Digits==5 ) point=point*10;

int n=1;

static int adr1,adr5,adr10,adr;

double s=0.0;

for(int i=1;i<=20;i++)

{

while(TimeDayOfWeek(iTime(NULL,PERIOD_D1,n))==0) n++;

s=s + ( iHigh(NULL,PERIOD_D1,n) - iLow(NULL,PERIOD_D1,n) )/point;

if(i==1) adr1=MathRound(s);

if(i==5) adr5=MathRound(s/5);

if(i==10) adr10=MathRound(s/10);

n++;

}

adr = MathRound((adr1+adr5+adr10)/3.0);

pls. also add a function to turn on/off for stuffs in yellow box...thanks!

--- 帖子 #1000 ---
A good example of using confluence for entry. Here we have price reversing before the AB=CD which is perfectly normal. In addition, the symmetry isn't very good.

The question is: How do we know when to enter or to start scaling in? Well, that's a question that each trader has to answer for himself. It's our responsibility to find a filtering system that gives us the best odds off success. For me it's still a personal journey. The possibilities are only limited by our imagination (and by our willingness to learn and work at it)

For me, I love my fibos and I'm beginning to love the Gann fan. In this example, 3 layers of confluence trumps the fact that we have poor symmetry and the fact that price hasn't reached he AB=CD completion level. Neither are a requirement for an entry.

NZD/JPY 4H CWW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Now, strip away everything from the chart and have a look at the fibo/Gann fan confluence, nearly to the pip. We have the BC extension 141fibo exactly at the larger move 78.6fibo exactly at the bottom range of the Gann fan. Coincidence? Maybe, maybe not. For me, just the sort of confluence that would give me the confidence to pull the trigger early instead of waiting for the AB=CD or waiting for a reversal and TDI cross. The TDI cross is 30 pips above the reversal point. In my opinion, you'd gain nothing by waiting except a higher risk entry with less potential. It's also important to note that you would already know where that green circle is going to be before price reaches that point. So if your mapping and tracking the trade with your filters already in place, you won't have to second guess yourself when the time comes for action. The last thing we want to do is fire from the hip like a wild west gunslinger. We want calculated, predetermined zones of entry.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

NOTE: The WW hasn't reached the target line by any means, and may never reach the target line but the reversal so far is a nice 40 pips giving us the opportunity to bank some pips and let the rest of the positions free roll. For expo, i think he's managing based on multiple positions. He entered one early, then scale in second position at worse price to average in. Then maybe third position at worser price to average in. If price took off with his all three positions and went to tp, he will hit a big home run. The problem with this is it's very complicated to me, I don't know how he calculate the risk percentage each trade and you might miss the big move if the price only took your first position and went to your take profit area. For me, i mostly enter based on risk percentage, for example, if i calculate the eurusd pair might be 12 pips sl, i divide by 5% for 12 pips. I mostly aim for 1 to 1 risk ratio only.

Comment on guys.

--- 帖子 #1011 ---
I am sorry if some seem unclear. As you can see they are marked as "private" charts which mean they can only be seen if I give the link (which I have here). As they were originally intended for my eyes only I haven't made them extremely clear, jusrt quickly drawn them so I can understand them when looking back on them later. Is there any specific one you want me to clarify?

I have read that Expo scales in/out of his positions and honestly I think that it is up to everyone to decide what they feel is best. Personally I never do. I put a limit order at the end of the AB=CD, put the stop a couple of pips below/above (depending on timeframe) and set my target at about 1-2.5RR (depending on S/R zones coming up). I don't go for more as I rather take many small wins than occasionally big ones. This limits the drawdown.

I do just like you do with the percentage of risk. I never risk more than 2-2.5% and divide that with the amount of pips to get the position size.

I hope this helped you, and nice setups you sent. I have found that past horizontal support/resistance zones at the sweet zone works like a charm when trading these patterns. A nice fibonacci retracement (38.2, 50 or 61.8%) as well and it's a solid trade.

Take care!

--- 帖子 #1050 ---
Hello Rees. You're welcome brother. God bless you and thanks for posting.

The "sweet" zone as depicted in this diagram is the area

where price breaks through the XB trend line down to the

parallel extension line of AC starting at point B. Sounds

complicated but if you look at the diagram, it's really not.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

If you use the indicator that "parviz" so graciously made for us, it basically will map out the sweet zone for you. I wish I had more time at home to explain, but I'll be away form my computer until morning again. Hopefully this helps.

Note: The reversal point D can be anywhere from the original trend line XB down to the yellow extension line. (and sometimes when there is strong momentum, even farther)

Here is a CWW that I entered at the end of last week. I ended up booking 100 pips. It's a good example of price reversing in the sweet zone exactly at the 200FIB extension of BC. Sweet zone highlighted as the blue triangle.

I drew this manually so you can hopefully see the realation to the diagram above

AUD/CHF 4H CWW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1053 ---
I'll try to understand this based on my observation. The X point is actually a very grey area. The more clearer the X point is, the stronger is the signal. In your chart, the X point is actually very forceful. You can say that it's there, you can say it's not. It really varies depends on how you define it. For me, it's not there because if you look further to the left of the chart, it was a nice upswing move. You were simply "forcing" an X there for the setup. Yes, if you switch to a smaller timeframe, it might be there but there's really no point trying to squeeze out a trade. ABCD was definitely there but not the X.

I think some examples from bill wolfe himself are also very unclear because he would simply find those charts with weird X placement. Of course, they worked because they were cherry picking them.

In fact, the chart you posted looked like a gartley pattern.

Anyway, correct me if i am wrong. Still learning also.

--- 帖子 #1101 ---
That's a great question and I think it depends on any local confluence. I tend to stay on the side lines when I can't see any real immediate confluence. Especially when the CD leg is beyond the completion level. Also, I think the time frame has a lot to do with it. On this WW it would be reasonable to have a 200 pip SL if we were targeting a 600+ pip TP. (better have super small positions though!) Remember the original theory that Mr. Wolfe stated was based on the "physics" of the wave. For each action there is an equal and opposite reaction. Imagine an elastic band being stretched to the point where the momentum finally stops and then releasing all that stored up energy back in the opposite direction. In relating that to a daily price chart, well, it may take a few weeks for price to run out of momentum and re-balance itself. Unfortunately that may be 200+ pips, hence the super small positions and the scale in option.

We've talked about this WW before.

Sorry my chart is a little busy. In analyzing this wave I see that original big booming bullish candle a couple of weeks ago pushing price right into the AB=CD zone, which also happened to be the 200FIB extension of BC and the 61.8FIB from the overall bigger move. Immediately 100 pip re trace. Then looks like a couple of weeks of accumulation.

No we are testing the BC extension 241FIB. In looking at the Gann Fan and the fact that we are now through the 61.8FIB, it looks like 131 may be in play. Any thoughts of me getting short now are off the table.

I would now only consider scaling in short from 130.50-131.50

--- 帖子 #1110 ---
Hi Guran01.

The first thing you need to know is that the Gann fan I'm using is actually the Fib Fan tool with modified inputs. I'm fairly inexperienced at using Gann fans but from doing some research it's necessary to have you're chart "squared" so the levels stay true.

Basically, you need to put a fib fan on your chart and then add these levels and description (the levels are the angles that have been converted into radians)

Then, use the "trend line by angle" tool to put a 45 degree line on your chart from the starting point you want to use. Then use that new modified fib fan and make sure the 1x1 line is on the 45 degree line.

Where you draw them is subjective. Bigger time frames I believe carry more significance.

I made this chart so it would be easy for anyone interested.Here are the levels you need to add to your fib fan tool with matching descriptions:
Attached Image

I know this chart is a bit cluttered but here is an example of one I'm looking at for this week. I have one fan from the bigger wave down and one from the most recent wave down

EUR/GBP 4H CWW SET UP
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

I forgot to mention how it is working:

1) It automatically looks and find every possible CWW (Potential and Completed), for all 6 ExtDepth that you entered in the input.

2)It draws all findings on the same chart and assign a clickable button for each of them.

3) you can view and have the characteristic of any of them by clicking its button.

4)Since the indicator halts after each new run, whenever you like you can force it to research again by clicking the corresponding "SEARCH AGAIN" button.

--- 帖子 #1125 ---
Hi Kurt:

Finally I have found the bug causing inconsistency between the version 8.5 and trial version , it was in closure of one "For loop" ,which was different .

Here i explain now, how the points X to D is selected and analysed, i believe that this will answer all of your questions, which i was not able to clarify before correctly:

1)After zigzag finish, program select the last 5 point in the array, and check them for any valid CWW(both potential and completed), if found then, it move to the next ExtDepth.

2) If it does not find any then, it would shift all X to D point one zigzag value to the left and look for a valid CWW , and it will continue to do that, for 5 times (which at the end of this loop, the first D point has replaced the first X), meanwhile if at any point it find any CWW,it draw it and skip to the next depth.

3) If even after these 5 shift again it does not find any CWW again it will go to the next depth.

4) making the long discussion short, it does not look for the last 5 zigzag values ,but instead in the last 10 value, and for five times, i would say.

I hope that this explanation was simple enough for every one to understand.

Soon i will post a bug free version of the last indicator.

Hi kurt:

The problem of a shifting of zigzag line was because the indicator was stopping when it search all the depth once.

In this version , program is always running and it does not stop to find new CWW (and so will repaint ), unless you press any of the button to view a specific one , once you click any of these buttons the indicator halts,and let you do your analysis on the drawing, when you are finished with it, then just pressing the "Search Again" will restart the indicator.(in this picture of you, the problem has appeared because the program was in Halt and did not redraw)

Hi kurt and everybody:

Since this last version, is always running and do a lot of calculation on each run, it would use a lot of your CPU time, especially if multiple instances of it are on different pairs , so i suggest as soon as it finds the patterns , press one of the buttons so that program stop searching , and if you need it again, rerun it by clicking "search again" button, this way your computer will not be slow.

The indicator couldn't pick this one up because the D leg was too choppy, but I've been tracking this one manually for a couple of weeks. Most traders would ask why try to catch a falling knife. Well, I've always been a contrarian trader and probably always will be.

Anyways, here's the theory behind the madness.

1) AB=CD symmetry of length perfectly matches up with the 200FIB extension of BC

2) AB=CD candle symmetry is also very good

3) AB=CD completion also happens to be right at the 4x1 Gann fan level. Gann levels bring in the element of time which to me is very powerful.

4) AB=CD completion level is also about 20 pips from the completion of a Quasimodo pattern (sounds pretty fancy huh)

Anyways, the Aussie fundamentals of late have been less than desirable. Accordingly price has been under pressure for the last 6 weeks. However,I think this trade offers good risk reward value.

545 downloads

How to set up:

1. Drop the EA file in the "mql4/Experts" folder

2. Start MT4, open a 1m chart of any pair (example EURUSD)

3. Drag and drop the renko EA from the expert list on the EURUSD 1m chart

4. A text note should appears saying something like "open offline chart M2 EURUSD"

5. File -> Open offline chart -> select the time frame as shown by the EA (EURUSD M2)

--- 帖子 #1240 ---
Hi mate.

You're "X" point is in the wrong place. Based on that point, then line XB and AC are diverging. To be a valid Wolfe wave those two lines need to be converging.

It might not seem like much of a difference, but it really is. For one, the valid wave that I posted below has the "D" point about 10 pips lower than yours. As a result, any fibo analysis or any other confluence analysis may not be valid or consistent within the parameters of Wolfe wave theory. Keep practicing and posting my friend and it will become very natural and easy

Also, this is where Parviz' indicator is so useful. Just put it on the chart, fiddle with the zig zag setting and BOOM, there is the valid wave

See below where the starting point "X" should be

Cheers
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1255 ---
The latest stable versions of parvizCww indicator are 3, each with different characteristics:

1)version 8.5: Is a manual one, you click the button and select which depth and either complete or potential CWW is what you want.

2)version 9.6: Is automated one, it looks for all possible combination and when it finds them draw a button for each so that you may select which one you are interested in, and it shows you its characteristics. In this version when the indicator find all the possible patterns, it stops and does look for them only once, if you want to see the latest ones press "Search Again" button .(indicator does not repaint)

3)version 9.6.1: Basically is the same as 9.6, except that, it does not stop searching after finding CWW, and always look for new ones as they are developing and thus "Repaint", if you want to halt the program, by clicking button for any pattern, program stop searching and so you can examine the selected pattern as long as you want, without losing it, if it find a new pattern. By clicking "Search Again" button,you may restart the indicator again.(this version uses a lot of the CPU time,since it is always running and doing a lot of calculations .)

I ask kurt ,if it is possible ,to put all these versions in the first post, plus this explanation to help all the users.

Anatomy of a trade before an important news event.

This morning's US CPI and retail sales prints could potentially move the market 30-50 pips. Maybe it won't but that's not the point. I'm neither bearish nor bullish on USD/JPY which in essence for me is irrelevant. My strategy is to be prepared and waiting for the price to come into my zone. I never want to be scrambling at the last minute trying to initiate a trade by just shooting form the hip like a wild west gunslinger. This is a methodical method planned in advance. All I have to do is sit back and wait. In the meantime, if the WW breaks down, I just cancel all the orders and forget about it.

Basically, I am hoping the US data disappoints and becomes the catalyst for a price spike down into my zone.

NOTE: The most important aspect of the trade is where to put the limit orders and where to put the SLs. The trade needs room to breath, especially if you're trying to fill up orders on a news spike. The TPs are preset but not really important at this point. They are subject to micromanagement if/when the trade goes in my favor.

--- 帖子 #1282 ---
Hope everyone is enjoying their weekend.

Thought I'd get this week started by going through my pre-trade filtering process. There is no right or wrong way to do this. The process should be personal, but it needs to be done every time you take a trade.

Ok, so you put the WW indicator on a chart and you see a potential WW. In our example, the wave is pretty steep, a little rough around the edges, nothing too special. Just one of dozens and dozens of WWs that are forming during the week. So, why would we choose to trade or not trade this wave? Well, we can't answer that question without going through our personal filtering process.

Below is the potential wave without any filters. Just the naked wave detected by the indicator.

NZD/CAD 1H POTENTIAL CWW - NAKED
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

THE FILTERING PROCESS

I always check 4 things no matter what when I detect a potential wave. Again, each trader has their own set of tools. I have many, but these 4 are checked before EVERY trade.

1) Previous S/R

2) The BC extension FIB

3) The FIB retracement levels from the larger, most recent move

4) The Gann Fan

In our example, I've taken all of the structure trend lines off the chart along with the zig zag just so that it's easier to see the filters and comments. I started naked with only the two blue triangles that outline the potential wave. Then I added the filters

Here is the final chart with analysis below:

NZD/CAD 1H POTENTIAL CWW - WITH FILTERS
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

1) Notice the previous S/R. What sticks out most to me is the fact that price seems to accelerate when it's passing through resistance levels 1 and 2. So it stands to reason IF price breaks through resistance level 1, then it may accelerate towards level 2. Notice each time price moved through this zone, there are pretty large candles. This is a good thing. We want price to reach point D. Even better if it's accelerating. Remember the physics theory that Bill Wolfe quoted: "for every action there is an equal and opposite reaction". And that's what we want. We want that elastic band to stretch to the limit (point D) before running out of momentum, then all of that stored up energy can be released in the opposite direction, the direction of our trade.

2) Point D is exactly the 261.8FIB extension of BC

3) Point D is exactly the 61.8FIB retracement level of the biggest and most recent move

4) The 2x1 Gann fan line exactly intersects at point D. Remember Gann fans bring in the element of time. The only way point D can intersect that Gann line perfectly is if the CD leg of the wave has the same number of candles as the AB leg (again time is of the essence here) Remember the indicator draws the waves assuming it will have perfect candle symmetry between AB and CD. It looks like about 14 candles for the AB leg so price would have to reach point D in about 14 hours from market open to be exactly in that D circle. (That would be pretty amazing if you ask me). Still, a few hours less or more and it would be fairly close.

NOTE: Resistance level 2 is basically in line with our 2 confluent FIB levels.

Sorry if this seems like an endless rant, but I feel it's absolutely vital to trading these waves successfully. I hope traders will take the time to look at the chart and compare it to what I'm saying. Look at the first chart. Looks like random price action. Put WW theory and a filtering system in place and you get chart 2. Now price doesn't look quite that random.

Also note, I will be scaling in a bit early as I like to do. Probably 5 positions 2-3 pips apart. With seemingly so much resistance heading into point D, I like to make sure I get at least a few small positions filled.

Having gone through all of this analysis, the market could open up tomorrow and price could just drift lower and completely invalidate this wave before it actually comes to fruition. Or, price could make it to D and then an OPEC member could unexpectedly make a statement that they are increasing supply, thus oil price plummets, thus sending NZD/CAD price 100 pips higher blowing up our trade. Both scenarios are irrelevant to our plan. We can't predict if price will go lower tomorrow and we can't predict what an OPEC member will unexpectedly say. What we can do, is locate a high probability zone where price may reverse based on Wolfe wave theory coupled with a well thought out filtering system.

I hope this post will open trader's eyes to the possibilities. You are only limited by your imagination and your willingness to do the hard work. Be meticulous, be patient, and be confident that your trading endeavors will become reality.

Remember, CONFLUENCE IS KING!

Safe and prosperous trading going forward friends.

-Kurt

--- 帖子 #1284 ---
@ Expo

You may, in time, want to think about putting a reference or link (is that possible?) to your excellent post 1286 on the front page of the thread.  IMHO, a strategy for filtering out high probability trades is exactly what the doctor ordered for the Wolfe Wave strategy given that so many trading opportunities set up.  The key is to look for highly visible support and resistance levels and you have the nearest ones covered with your resistance zones.  The confluence effect cannot be stressed enough and you have done a fabulous job of giving Wolfe Wave traders some boxes to tick so that they may have confidence in taking any particular trade.  Good job, sir!  After all, institutions move the markets and the likelihood of them trading Wolfe Waves is remote at best.  Therefore, in order to get your strategy trade moving, there has to be really good reasons why other participants would enter the market and propel it to your profit targets.  Confluence obviously gives more reasons why others would enter the market.

I have been developing my own price action strategy for some time now and have dissected trade set ups into their various components based on things that I want to watch out for. For instance if I'm looking at the various characteristics of a pullback in a trend, some things I may look for would be 50% pullback (0 or 1) or a pullback to the 20ema (o or 1). Using an Excel spreadsheet for this analysis is extremely powerful as, by the time one has looked at 200 trades or so with many criteria for each trade based on prior price action and the pullback sequence as well as entry, exit, win, lose, R-multiple profit (and loss - which should not exceed 1!), there is a good bit of data that can be queried in whatever way you like. The results can be very surprising and give the trader a few really key features to look for in order to find trades that have as much as  60-75% probability.  I would suggest, if other traders can be bothered, that a similar type of analysis is carried out for Wolfe Waves.  Criteria such as those in Expo's filtering system would be a good start to the column headings / criteria, but there could be many others too - again your imagination is the only thing limiting the process.  This type of exercise also ensures the trader records all of his/her trades and gives the trader a great deal of exposure to different looking set ups. It is easy to do manual backtesting on this type of strategy too, albeit time-consuming.  It is a marathon, not a sprint....

From a Price action perspective I really like the USDJPY setup that was posted (Expo I think) last week; for example, there is a bull channel on the H4 / H8 and price has pulled back to the trend line and also had a >50% PB from the high of the move.  There are other reasons too, but for me there is great confluence there.

Wishing you all a very profitable week ahead.

Stuart

--- 帖子 #1285 ---
Thanks Juri.

Yes, I draw the 45 degree line from the beginning of an impulse wave that I deem has relevance to area of interest.I think drawing the Gann fan is subjective to some extent. In the NZD/CAD example it's pretty obvious where it should be drawn. In many cases, however, the last impulse wave isn't so distinct. Many times I draw multiple fans just to see if any patterns emerge. I also like to check the higher time frames.

I'm still a novice when it comes to Gann fans but from what I've researched, it's hard to truly square time and price on the Meta 4 platform. I use the Fibonacci fan tool and add all of the levels manually with the corresponding converted angles. The fan doesn't stayed squared when changing time frames or when you're zooming in and out but it will remain squared when you go back to the original time frame and when you zoom back to where you originally drew the fan.

These are the converted angles with corresponding levels that I manually set in the Fibonacci fan tool
Attached Image

Hi Kurt,

Actually, I generally trade the FTSE (UKX) 5min chart so my strategy evolution and analysis is based on a couple of years of those charts plus another timeframe.  The aim is to get it going well on that and then move on to the infinitely more liquid EURUSD as and when I have looked into the idiosyncracies of that instrument on the 5min timeframe.  Currently getting all of the relevant charts saved when I can.  Every instrument has its own behavior in terms of what works well as technical S / R, how deep the pullbacks are - including how much a genuinely sensible stop might be taken out by before the move continues etc etc.  However, your post regarding the USDJPY Wolfe Wave spurred me to take a look at the setup and has got me doing a reasonable amount of work over the weekend on higher timeframe Fx charts to see if I can add them to my strategy trade plan.  TBH I would have liked to have seen the pullback go a little deeper (at least to 11313 which would be a double bottom on the H8 according to ProRealTime charts) as I can't see any robust technical support that has kicked in yet on the H8 apart from (with rose-tinted spectacles) maybe an inferred breakout test of a lower timeframe swing high pivot (11330) based on an upper tail .  I can see it on lower timeframe charts, but I generally like to at least be able to strongly  infer it on the timeframe that I am trading (tails on bars etc).  I'm thinking that we will maybe get another small leg down, but a swing stop should contain it if the bull trend on this timeframe is to continue.

The spreadsheet is time-consuming, but it is as ongoing dynamic piece of work so it doesn't have to feel like an arduous task.  Even starting one now, after a bit of thought as to what one wants to look for, and updating it with real-time trades rather than 'boring' backtesting may soon give enough data to become statistically significant for Wolfe Wavers.  The power of this approach should not be underestimated!

Also FWIW, I see your 'bearish Quasimodo pattern' - sorry, never heard of it! - as an expanding triangle or I believe some people call it a megaphone (?) where there is a concurrent bull trend (Higher highs) and bear trend (lower lows) and therefore a trading range.   I would generally expect the prior HH to be taken out given the strength of the bull spike at the start of the 4th leg, but the market is full of surprises and I may very well be wrong.

Green pips to all.

Stuart

--- 帖子 #1292 ---
What I mean is that when you change time frames or zoom in/out the 45 degree line will stay at 45 degrees but the 1x1 fan line won't stay on that 45 degree line

With the Meta 4 platform, the reality is that you can't truly square your Gann fan using the Fib fan tool. At least that's what it seems from reading all of the information I could find on the subject. At the very least, I just want the fan to come back to the same original position after changing time frames and zooming in/out so I don't have to redraw the 45 degree line and the Fib fan all over again.

There's a good discussion here by "Mastermind" whose knowledge on the subject dwarfs anything I could ever know. Post #8 is where the discussion starts.

https://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=652723

--- 帖子 #1299 ---
Just thought I'd mention this in case anyone else is experiencing computer lag due to have many charts up at once all with the WW indicator on them.

I have a fairly new computer but still experience lag and freezing and I'm using the 8.5 version. So after I go through my analysis for a particular pair, I just put the 2 triangles on the chart manually. Basically, I just use the WW that is already there from the indicator and superimpose two triangles onto the chart using the triangle drawing tool. Then I just delete the indicator from that chart. Whats left is all of the other filters and the two WW triangles. Now I can move onto another pair and not have to worry about any lag.

--- 帖子 #1358 ---
Yeah, the concept of the sweet zone is the masterpiece of Bill Wolfe IMHO, it combines time and space, allowing zero drawdown entries on narrow zones. He suggests beginners to trade those narrow ones, as those are much easier to handle from the risk perspective. Steep zones require other filters like harmonic completions (AB=CD), fib extensions, market structure, etc... since price can go quite a bit before snapping back to equilibrium.

Some thoughts about what makes up the sweet zone and the difference between AB=CD trading and WW trading.

Why is the sweet zone much more powerful in timing entries?

--- 帖子 #1375 ---
Is anyone using parviz Indicator? how do I know what the correct depth setting I should be using is?

--- 帖子 #1376 ---
Hi Golden.

There is no "correct" extdepth setting. The latest versions of the indicator (9.6 and 9.6.1) both automatically search all time frames and all extdepth settings. When it's done with the search, it will show clickable "buttons" that reveal the waves it has found. You can then click on the button to see the wave it has detected.

The older version 8.5 does not automatically search for Wolfe waves. The user has to select the time frame and the extdepth setting manually.

Many waves that have extremely choppy price action can not be detected by the indicator regardless of what the extdepth setting is on. Thus, it is beneficial to be able to detect and plot on Wolfe waves manually.

Just in case you haven't seen it, on post #1 the developer of the indicator, "parviz1953" has attached instructions for each of the 3 versions I mentioned above. Hopefully, he will correct me if I've made any mistakes explaining how the indicators work.

If you have any other questions, please feel free to ask. In the meantime, best of luck to you and thanks for posting.

Hope this helps.

Cheers, -Kurt

--- 帖子 #1385 ---
The NZD/USD was a valid WW. The question is how big of a stop loss is one willing to risk given the position size, The bigger question is why one would be inclined to trade this wave in the first place. In hindsight, everything is easy.

For this wave, what we can say before it reached point"D" was that the price action between A,B and C was a mess. Very choppy, with a couple of big wicks. Not good symmetry. Ideally we are looking for nice clean legs to our wave. Very distinct and uniform.

As an example, look at the price action on this developing WW. Fairly uniform from A to B, from B to C, and now on the way down to D. (although price seems to have stalled for a few days. A much cleaner wave

CAD/CHF DAILY WW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Not sure why 9.6 doesn't draw the correct "D" point. If you calculate it manually, D should be at about 1.1288 as it is shown by the 8.5 version. --- 帖子 #1409 ---
Hi :

Both version will draw the completed CWW and accept it as a valid complete , as soon as price reach the line1_3, and update every time you search again if price goes higher, if the price pass the 2nd sweet zone then, it does not draw it anymore( or show it as a potential) , and consider it a failed "complete" one.

PS:

So for a completed CWW, it does not wait for AB=CD ,and consider it valid by touch of Line1_3.

In contrast to "potential", which it calculate, and predict the D, on the basis of AB=CD.

The difference between U2 graph and yours , is that you used potential wave button and he chose the completed wave.

--- 帖子 #1426 ---
Hi Stuart.

Placing the SLs is going to be somewhat subjective. A lot will depend on your risk management profile. For me, I tend to use the FIB extension of BC as a guideline. So, if I'm planning on scaling in from the 161FIB to the 200FIB, then my SLs will be above/below the next level which would be the 261FIB. I also look at the XA FIB extension to see if there is any confluence. I also look at the FIB levels from the bigger move to see if there is any confluence. In addition, I also look at previous S/R and Gann fans. I'm trying to use multiple tools to find a layer of confluential resistance. Where is a level that will be the line in the sand? Then place my SLs above/below that level. The idea is to give the trade enough room to breath while managing the risk in a way that makes sense.

Here's an example form my active Kiwi trade. I took the trade levels and indicator off the chart so it's easier to see how I initially set my SLs. Hopefully, it's self explanatory. In this case the SL is roughly 30 pips from the top of the scale in zone which may seem like a lot for a 30MIN WW, but my ultimate TP zone is from 50-100 pips. As long as the total %risk for the trade is within my own personal risk management parameters, then I can sleep well at night.

It may sound silly to some, but for me, the whole process is almost an art form. From locating/mapping the wave, to constructing a confluence profile, to setting the SLs and TPs. It's all a personal journey. We all have the same canvas but we have the freedom to paint our own masterpiece (wow, that is some cheesy stuff right there!)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Updated look with trade levels and SLs moved to BE. Notice the 23.6FIB from the larger move is now my support area. The SLs at BE are just below that level. Now it's a stress free trade, just sit back and see if we hot a home run. I actually did bank some pips from one position. There were 7 scaled in from the start with 6 left running.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Just to take the discussion a little further, there is now a new bearish WW developing. This may give us a new guideline for adjusting a few of our TPs. Have a look here:
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1443 ---
Hi :

1) It would be much faster if you do not press "search again" button , instead change the TF and return , this will stop indicator and reinitialize , and so it is much faster.

2)The lower the TF the higher the amount of bars and data, so the slower the indicator.

3) I have implemented your idea : in this version you are not limited to a set of 6 ExtDepth anymore , you may now enter whatever you want (eg. 12,20 or 12,6,30,20) in the input. (only need to be comma separated, does not even need to be in order).

This will replace version 9.6 .

--- 帖子 #1492 ---
Hey Kurt,

I use IG index and their free access to ProRealTime charts.  That is why I struggled to take a look at Parviz' indicator so had to set up a demo account just to check it out.

With respect to the chart timeframes, I dislike the differences.  As I trade FTSE price action on lower timeframes I really like the 8am open and the 16:30 close because it gives the day a certain structure.  The globex session drives me nuts as some of the daily price action is affected by the globex session, whereas channels and patterns often carry though from the close of the prior day to the open of 'today' and you don't see that if you have the globex chart up so it is generally more work than it should be to rationalise the price action.  I have come to the conclusion that it shouldn't matter because whichever chart is being traded needs to make sense so if a daily session channel line is providing support, there is always another reason that should be apparent on the globex chart.  Ok, so I've gone off on one a bit there - sorry!  The message I guess is that it shouldn't matter.  Gaps are just spikes, climaxes, trend bars.  I just mentally fill in the gaps with a trend bar. I could probably elaborate on that at some point if you wanted me to.

Yes, I've seen the discussion about what constitutes a valid start point or point X and can see that it is in the eye of the beholder and neither way is right or wrong.  If it works for 'you' then it is right for you.  I wasn't actually looking for Wolfe Waves when I saw this GBPJPY possibility; I was looking through some HTF charts trying to identify potential setups for a different strategy and then I noticed this WW setup so maybe it doesn't look as appealing to a WW trader, but from a PA perspective there's the potential to structure some nice trades.

Cheers

Stuart

--- 帖子 #1494 ---
Hi there and welcome to Expo's quality WW thread!

It has been said that people don't trade the markets; they trade their beliefs about the markets.  So first you have to ask yourself if you believe that Fib numbers have any use in the markets.  If you do then you can probably trade them, but ask yourself why do you believe in them.  I know that Expo, or Kurt, among many others believe in these % extensions (that for some reason get labeled as Fibos but I'm not sure what the numbers actually have to do with Fibonacci sequence!- if they do then can someone please enlighten me) and from what I have seen they are useful to them and can help traders who believe in them to attach a structure to their trading set ups with respect to how they scale in to trades or where they place their stops. This is a powerful thing, as a strategy and set up you believe in and can trade without question is worth its weight in gold. I am probably in the minority of traders who don't find 'Fib' numbers useful in their trading because they don't have any statistical significance and are as good as / no better than any other numbers you may care to conjur up. That is my belief and you may not find it useful.  I believe that looking for support and resistance levels and zones to the left on the chart and trying to find areas of confluence with forms of  leg 1 =leg 2 (measured) moves - these are areas of self-fulfilling prophecies that generate their own support / resistance because bulls will go long / buy back their shorts and at the same time bears will go short / sell out of their longs  - in the recent past gives the best chance of success and I use these areas to structure my trades.

I do not mean to antagonise anyone and I make no judgement on what other people believe.  There are many ways to trade in general and certainly many ways to trade Wolfe Waves.  'Fibos' may provide you with the answer, but if they don't then it is certainly possible trade without them.

Cheers,

Stuart

--- 帖子 #1496 ---
Nice post Sal. It's always productive and educational to here some views from the other side of the coin sort of speak. By the way, I thought your charts looked familiar. I had recently downloaded the trial platform to check out their renko options.

The extensions come from the true retracement levels that are derived from the actual fibonacci number sequence.

Here's a copy and past from this pdf: http://www.forex.com/uk/pdf/Fibonacci-guide.pdf

Maybe of some interest to others, just thought I'd post it here.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

If you use the legitimate retracement levels derived form the # sequence: .236, .382, .618. and you come up with the default meta4 extension levels.

1/.236 = 4.23

1/.382 = 2.61

1/.618 = 1.61

The rest are derived from the added levels thru squaring , etc etc. There are entire books written on the subject but not really something we need to get into for our purposes.

Anyways, more importantly, as you stated, we need to be looking left to see the previous S/R. My love affair with fibos/extensions comes when multiple levels match up with those previous S/R levels.

.

I believe that human behavior is at the root of price action. How and why that behavior is shaped could come from a myriad of reasons from technicals, to fundamentals, to order flow, to insider trading, to HFTs, to reasons beyond the scope of our knowledge. For me, if Fibo spirals can exactly model physical nature, then it's my belief that Fibo levels can model traders behavior (to some extent). Anyways, probably beyond the scope of this thread, just rambling on. I suppose there are Fibomaniacs and then there are anti-Fibites, lol.

I'll try to give an example here in a little while when I get a moment.

--- 帖子 #1497 ---
PREVIOUS S/R with FIBONACCI retracement/extension analysis

Sorry if the chart is a little busy with 4 different fibos but I wanted to show the whole picture. If even one trader finds this post useful, then it's worth posting.

NZD/JPY 4H POTENTIAL CWW
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Lets try and break it down. Others may see it differently, and that's a good thing. This is how I see it. Note, the AB=CD is basically about 80.60

THE THOUGHT PROCESS

1) If price actually continues higher on the D leg, then based on previous S/R and the psychological round number theory, 80.00 should be a big hurdle as far as resistance goes. But let's assume for the moment that price does indeed break through that psychological 80 level, now what?

2) The 61.8 FIB retracement level is basically within 10 pips of the AB=CD price. Remember, we are talking about a structure that spans over 400 pips and a retracement that started 4 months ago.

3) The 141.4FIB extension of MH (major high) is within a few pips of AB=CD

4) The 200FIB extension of XA is 13 pips from AB=CD

5) The 361FIB extension of BC is 17 pips from AB=CD

Ok so what, a bunch of meaningless FIB retrace/extension levels just happen to be in the area of AB=CD. well, not so fast lets look a bit deeper.

6) The acceleration zone - looking left you really don't see any previous important S/R in this zone. So, in my opinion, if price does indeed break through the 80 barrier, then there may be one last impulse wave as price gets into the acceleration zone.

Here's the kicker. When you look back to the right from the acceleration zone you see basically nothing in the way of FIB levels. Interesting to say the least considering we are talking about a 50 pip zone. Instead, all of the most recent and most pertinent FIB levels are all piling up right around that AB=CD level. Coincidence?

7) And finally, it is pretty clear where the major supply level is at (major resistance)

So the only question is where to enter into this trade if it so happens that price does penetrate into what I am calling the "acceleration zone".

For me, there is no need to get to cute here. I'm not trying to pick tops/bottoms. I'm trying to pick zones that have a high probably of a price reversal. From the chart, you can see the scale in zone. I will likely use my scaling in script to set up about 10 small positions about 3-4 pips apart. Maybe even 20 smaller positions 2 pips apart.

Sorry if this seemed like an endless rant. Hope it helps someone in some small way. I know it helps me.

Cheers to a great week ahead -Kurt

--- 帖子 #1516 ---
Overall, I have been trading for about 10 years. I've dabbled in dozens of systems and blown many small accounts. I basically refused to take responsibility for my losses.

About 15 months ago I started studying Wolfe waves. I spent about 6 months using a demo account to see what worked and what didn't. Learning the structure was the easy part, learning how to apply the theory was the hard part. Not because it's really complicated, but because we each have a personality profile when it comes to trading. In my opinion, the biggest hurdle to overcome in trading is yourself. Mainly your ego, your fears, and your greed. Like many I put my 10,000 hours of study in to be a successful trader, but that means nothing if you can't tame the beast that lies inside all of us.

Anyways, I've been trading mainly WWs for about 9 months now. It's hard to quantify how many pips a month as I tend to scale in from 3-40 positions per trade depending on the time frame and pair. So the number of pips per month isn't really that relevant. What's relevant is consistently initiating high probability trades with sound risk management. I put up a trade explorer 14 days ago for a mini account and it shows nearly +10,000 pips, which doesn't really mean too much considering how many micro positions were scaled in. With my overall account size, I'm happy to harvest 20-50 pips a day. That's more than enough to live comfortably given my monthly financial obligations. As my overall account grows, it will become irrelevant. A few good trades a month can be very lucrative once the account grows to a certain level. For me, it was never about the money, it was always about the freedom. And honestly, I love the competition, the chase, the hunt, the win. I grew up in a hockey family, that's all we ever did. We lived it, we breathed it. Every day was a war on the ice, and only the ones with the commitment and mental fortitude survived. Trading is no different. It's a tough game but I find it rewarding in many ways other than just the financial rewards.

Cheers, -Kurt

--- 帖子 #1534 ---
If you have read the thread , you know that there was a lot of controversies regarding the selection of X point, even in pdf of wolfe himself , but it has been agreed to comply with the expo preference (and of course many others.. ), that, a valid X point is better to be located between B and C points for a valid Classical WW. In your drawing ,X is way below B, and in contradiction to the rule C is above A, indeed you considered the body of the bar to fit the WW, if you take the wicks into account then you see that C is higher than A.

--- 帖子 #1544 ---
money management, for EX.

case1

You have 5 winners on M15 which gives you +1000 pips and 1 loser on D1 which costs you -1200 pips.

case2

You have 5 losers on M15 which costs you -1000 pips and 1 winner on D1 which gives you +1200 pips.

whatever case happens, it will make your equity curve unstable... there must be a solution and let's work it out~

--- 帖子 #1545 ---
The time frame and number of pips is irrelevant.

If you risk 1% per trade then a losing trade costs you 1% of your account.

Smaller time frame, smaller stop loss, bigger position

Bigger time frame, bigger stop loss, smaller position

Both scenarios will have the same predetermined risk of 1%

Hello traders. Looking forward to an exciting week ahead. Should be many good opportunities.

I have been fiddling around with the "zup" harmonic indicator over the weekend and will be adding it to my toolbox. I have seen the "zup" versions in the past but never really used them. For more experienced traders here, this might be of some use.

Basically, I am just adding the indicator to my chart to see if any Wolfe waves correspond with the end point of a larger harmonic structure. (it's inevitable that some will). Another aspect is multi time frame analysis. For instance, the zup shows a bearish gartley on the daily and the there is a WW with the same ending point on a smaller time frame.

Anyways, just thinking and and sharing out loud. I have been fiddling with the settings just for aesthetics and plan on delving more deeply into this indicator. The thread's focus is still on Wolfe waves, just adding another layer to the cake.

I believe member "poruchik" is the resident expert on this indicator. He has added some very useful and relevant posts here already.

Cheers all, green pips going forward, -Kurt

Here's just one example. A bullish bat with basically the same end point as the Wolfe wave. Remember, we are generally talking about price "zones" not an exact price.

--- 帖子 #1637 ---
Refer to the diagram on post #1.

For a bullish WW, after point X and A are established, you are looking for B as a lower low, then C as a lower high, then D as another lower low that breaks the trend line formed by XB.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1640 ---
A couple of points.

1) I don't think this is a major reversal for NZD/CHF which is basically irrelevant anyways. I'm only looking for a short term price correction based on WW theory. In this case, based on the time frame and the actual structure, price may correct 30-50 pips.

2) I don't set my TPs at the actual "target line" or try to correlate a TP with the "estimated time of arrival". I'm generally very conservative with my TPs, taking profits (or at least partial profits) before the actual target line. As was the case with my last NZD/CHF trade. No need to get greedy, especially heading into Friday. The ETA price was about 15-20 pips lower but I like to get out a bit early and stay away from the herd mentality. We don't need home run trades. They're nice but not really needed. With a 10k account, making 30 pips a day, trading only 1 lot per 10k of capital, and you'll be financially free in one year.

--- 帖子 #1643 ---
Well, they're ALL worth watching, but is it worth trading?

Price goes where it wants to go, so the question is why might price reverse or correct other than just the simple fact that it has reached the WW sweet zone?

Is there FIB confluence? Is there previous S/R? Bollinger band breaks? Pertinent Gann fan level? Divergence? Risk off sentiment? GDT results due out soon? Is there anything other than price entering the sweet zone that can potentially make this trade have a higher probability of success?

Every trader has a different perspective and a different set of tools. It's our job as traders to utilize our personal toolbox coupled with our unique perspective to give us the "edge" needed to be successful in this business.

--- 帖子 #1651 ---
Here is a good example.

THE FIRST WW: Leg CD has uniform price action down to the sweet zone D. As a result, there is very nice symmetry and would be a wave I would like to trade.

THE SECOND WW: Leg CD has sideways price action. Price has not dropped below point C so technically this is still a valid WW. However, the wave structure is indecisive and any subsequent move to point D will exhibit very poor wave symmetry. As such, this set up would go into the scrap heap.

Hope this example helps

GPY/JPY 15MIN CWW EXAMPLES
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1654 ---
When I first started studying WWs, that's exactly what I would do. Now, there's a group of indicator's developed by member "parviz 1953" that automatically search and detect CWWs. The different versions and instructions can be found on post #1

However, there are no short cuts to being proficient at trading CWWs. Learning to spot and map out WWs manually is a necessary exercise if you want to truly be immersed in WW theory. I advise you to start at post #1 and read through the entire thread. There have been some excellent improvements made along the way and some very thoughtful and pertinent posts made by some very good traders.

Good luck!

-Kurt

--- 帖子 #1679 ---
You're welcome Eddy.

Finding the WWs is the same on all TFs. The "extdepth" setting is just used to make the zig zag fit the wave. A lot of times I can see the WW with the naked eye but the indicator isn't picking it up on certain settings. So I try different TFs and different extdepth settings to try and find the combination that will show the wave with the zig zag. Sometimes it may not be possible. No problem, I just draw them manually.

Greens pips. Boarding a plane in a few hours for vacation

Cheers, -Kurt

the answer is simple :

// put in extern variables section//

extern string CurrencyName = "EURUSD"; //or any pair you want//
extern int TimeFrame = 43200;

// placed somewhere within your code//
double PreviousClose = iClose (NULL, TimeFrame, 1);

MonthHigh = iHigh(Symbol(),PERIOD_MN1,43200,1);

MonthLow = iLow(Symbol(),PERIOD_MN1,43200,1);

MonthClose = iClose(Symbol(),PERIOD_MN1,43200,1);

or
double PreviousHigh = iHigh (CurrencyName, TimeFrame, 0);
double PreviousLow = iLow (CurrencyName, TimeFrame, 0);
double PreviousClose = iClose (CurrencyName, TimeFrame, 0);

cheers

Alex

--- 帖子 #1713 ---
Hi :

1)I am not sure what is your Question here. The third argument in the iHigh() function is the shift , it means Bar No. for which you want the function to return, its value, to you.

The last bar is zero the previous one is 1. So for previous month high ,the shift is 1 and MonthHigh = iHigh(Symbol(),PERIOD_MN1,1), and for two month ago it is iHigh(Symbol(),PERIOD_MN1,2).

2) if you need a function to return the number of minute of a time frame ,whatever notation that you send to it as a string argument ....

this little function may help:

int StringToTimeFrame(string tfs)

{

int tf=0;

if(tfs=="M1" || tfs=="1" ||tfs=="m1") tf=PERIOD_M1;

if(tfs=="M5" || tfs=="5" ||tfs=="m5") tf=PERIOD_M5;

if(tfs=="M15"|| tfs=="15" ||tfs=="m15") tf=PERIOD_M15;

if(tfs=="M30"|| tfs=="30" ||tfs=="m30") tf=PERIOD_M30;

if(tfs=="H1" || tfs=="60" ||tfs=="h1") tf=PERIOD_H1;

if(tfs=="H4" || tfs=="240" ||tfs=="h4") tf=PERIOD_H4;

if(tfs=="D1" || tfs=="1440" ||tfs=="d1") tf=PERIOD_D1;

if(tfs=="W1" || tfs=="10080" ||tfs=="w1") tf=PERIOD_W1;

if(tfs=="MN" || tfs=="43200" ||tfs=="mn") tf=PERIOD_MN1;

if(tf==0) tf=Period();

return(tf);

}

I hope this would help you.

sincerely parviz

Here is a brief introduction for EA:

1 XABCD Style

Once a CWW was found by Praviz's indi...We will draw a Fibo Extension on XA or BC( if BC is too short we use XA, if both are too short we use previous ZZ swing)

After you finished drawing, put EA into the chart and choose an Area you want to trade NEAR D Point.

In this case I choose 176.4-223.6, that means trade 2 lvls on 176.4 & 223.6...

EA will automatically find entry point and Draw XC line then set a time to stop.

So users only need to choose trading areas...EA will finish everything else for you.

--- 帖子 #1731 ---
Hi:

As i said the current bar is always the zero bar , and we can't use negative bar number for future bar eg.: Time[-30 ]; return error.

So you should calculate it indirectly like this for example:

future_bar_time=Time[0]+30*Period()*60;

this will give you time for the 30th bar after the current bar in seconds passed since 00:00 a.m. 1st of January 1970.

(Time[Bar No.] ,is a Series array that contains open time of each bar of the current chart.)

--- 帖子 #1745 ---
Hi Parviz,

I suspect Pipmaster is much like myself in that he trades price action from reading charts competently and taking discretionary trades (Pipmaster please correct me if I am wrong).  I have received the message loud and clear that this is probably not the correct 'place' / thread to promote those methods.  In any case, it is not something one can teach to a community easily.  Discretionary PA trading is an art / skill that is acquired over a very very long time and I would imagine that most (not all) people that follow this thread should not be advised to start trading in this way.  In order to do it successfully and consistently one has to understand risk, reward AND probability of a successful trade outcome.  Everyone can set a stop and a profit target (risk and reward) but relatively few traders understand the probability aspect ( ie the critical variable that determines whether they will have a mathematical edge or not) unless they either have a strategy where they have taken hundreds of trades and generated statistics or understand how to read charts.

Just an opinion.  I should point out that the GBPJPY move has been outlined from a Wolfe Wave perspective by both myself and (I think) Expo if you want to look at previous posts.

Cheers

Stuart

--- 帖子 #1750 ---
Trading is not supposed to be easy!  If it were easy then anyone with 'no talent' would be able to make money.  However, you are trying to take money from other smart traders (or computers) so you have to be, on average, smarter than them. That does not mean 'cleverer'.  There are many people out there who have brains the size of Jupiter who would not make good traders.  Nothing is certain and people do not like dealing with uncertainty.  This is why it is important to have an understanding of probability because trading is about consistently executing your positive expectancy plan in order to come out on top in the long term.  Any one particular trade is of no consequence, whether it be a winner or loser.  Each trade is just part of the plan and it is necessary to have losers in order to be able to have the (bigger) winners etc etc.   Anyone who has the right psychology, or can train themselves to have the right psychology can become a good trader. I'm still working on that part truth be told! If you want to make a living in any profession, you have to train and get good at whatever it is that you decide to do. One does not become an excellent accountant, lecturer, scientist, store-owner / business person overnight.  It takes time, effort and hard work and anyone who does not realise this and is not willing to put in the hard work deserves to lose.  It doesn't matter if you are trading an actual system/strategy like Wolfe Waves or if you are trading by purely reading the price action.  What you need is understanding.

Re: News - I pay absolutely no attention to news because I don't understand how to trade it and even if I did, the computers trading the news are far quicker than I could ever be.  Let the news happen, observe what the market is telling you and trade accordingly.

Re: Fibonacci - I have been through this before

Breakout / false break - all to do with reading the price action.  It IS hard, but you can increase your probability by letting the breakout succeed or fail.  If it succeeds, there will usually be a breakout pullback trade  where you can get in - usually at a worse price because you have gained probability so it must be paid for in risk.

etc

SO in short: Trading is gambling if you do not have a plan and do not understand what the chart in front of you is saying- agreed.  But, put the work, time, sweat, blood, tears into it and come up with a positive expectancy plan and you have a good chance of coming up with a something that can work, if you trade it properly and have worked on 'your' psychology.

--- 帖子 #1808 ---
Hi Shuo and thanks for posting

I am heading out the door very soon until tomorrow morning. So to give you a short answer I think the stop loss will be dependent a lot on your risk profile.

From a price action standpoint. I try and use the FIB extensions as a guide as well as previous S/R levels. It is always a work in progress. Recently, I have been studying supply/demand zones as a way to find prudent stop loss levels. I think each trader will see price action a bit differently so stop losses may be a personal style rather than a hard rule.

My main thought when placing stop losses is to make sure I give the trade enough room to breathe. I try and think where the market makers will likely be trying to blow up retail traders and then place my stop a bit farther above or below that level. If need be I just reduce my position size and use a bigger stop just to give my trade a little more breathing room without taking on anymore risk.

I hope this helps but I think it ultimately is a function of experience in finding out what works thru trial and error.

Good luck friend.

--- 帖子 #1847 ---
Hi Wiz.

Thanks for the compliments. My apologies for such a late response. I've been really busy lately.

I've always been intrigued by Renko charts. They appeal to my visual senses. My Wolfe wave journey is still a work in progress so I don't have all the answers.

For me the only potential downside to Renko when using them for WW analysis is that in many instances they show symmetry when in fact there is no symmetry. For example, when leg AB takes nearly the same number of candles to complete as leg CD. Since Renko is based on price and not time, you will see perfectly symmetrical Renko WWs that really aren't symmetrical when you look at the candlestick chart.

One thing I really like is how easy it is to see previous S/R, demand and supply zones, etc.

Here's a snapshot of the same WW, candlestick style and Renko side by side just to see the visual benefit of Renko.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Anyways, thanks for dropping by. I value any input you have. As I said from the start, this is still a work in progress. Unfortunately, I over committed myself in my local community until Christmas so the thread has been dying as of late. Starting in the new year I'll have free time to try and revive this thread.

Cheers mate, stay safe and stay green

Hi Parviz1955

Actually i would like to thank you for your great work in creating these indicators.

I have suggestions to develop indicator ver 9.7.2, ver 8.5 and ver 9.6.1

For Complete and potential patterns,

1- There is no need for green triangle , it is better to remove it or make it by user choice to make it on or off, we want to see easy clear chart.

For "Complete patterns only - we are interested more in stability of point d and profit targets ":

1- "As I understand these fibo values are changing as price moves - and only used to match with fibos shown in "search again" in case of complete pattern - and becomes fixed once price breaks top of green traingle, ash shown in chart 3 by yellow arrow ".

For shown fibo percentage , We do not need all these fibo and in such format, we need fibos for D point only

AB/XA =

CD/BD =

BC/AB =

CD/XA =

CD/AB =

BD/XA =
(a) I suggest to replace it by (in same format below with the ability to change text size )

D/XA =

D/Main =

"Main , is fibo from z1 z2 , which represents LL or HH before point x , as shown in attached chart"

D/BC =
(b) For Search again box :

(as i understand , these values are fixed and do not vary as price vary)
I- Each Fibo must be shown in a different color and line format to be easily to easily distinguish between lines on chart
II - I Suggest to only use the following fibos only:

XA FIBO

BC FIBO

Main (Z1Z2) FIBO
III - Add take profit points :

TP1 : "Value " Horizontal line from X point

TP2 : "Value " Horizontal line from C point

TP3 : "Value " Horizontal line from A point

For "Potential patterns only - we are interested in stability of point c":
1- "As I understand these fibo values are changing as price moves, and only used to match with fibos shown in "search again" in case of complete pattern ".

For shown fibo percentage , We do not need all these fibo and in such format, we need fibos for D point only

AB/XA =

CD/BD =

BC/AB =

CD/XA =

CD/AB =

BD/XA =
(a) I suggest to replace it by (in same format below with the ability to change text size )

C/XA =

C/Main1 =

"Main , is fibo from S1 S2 " As Shown in chart 2, which represents LL or HH before point x "

C/AB =

(b) For Search again box :

(as i understand , these values are fixed and do not vary as price vary)
I- Each Fibo must be shown in a different color and line format to be easily to easily distinguish between lines on chart
II - I Suggest to only use the following fibos only:
(for Point c):

C/XA =

C/Main1 =

"Main , is fibo from S1 S2 " As Shown in chart 2, which represents LL or HH before point x "

C/AB =
(For Point D)

D/XA FIBO

D/BC FIBO

D/Main (Z1Z2) FIBO as shown in chart 1

I am ready for any clarifications

Thank you in advance.

--- 帖子 #1900 ---
For the EUR/CAD Daily you posted I'm not a big fan of X just being a random location. I see traders just picking X anywhere just to fit in it for the Wolfe wave. For me point X should be distinct, either a swing Hi/Lo point or at least a minor localized Hi/Lo

If you look closely you can see that there actually was a valid classic bullish Wolfe wave that already has played out. Price rejected for a week straight at the 200FIB extension which was only 30 pips from perfect AB=CD completion. Not bad considering the impulse waves were over 500 pips each. Price then re-traced about 600 pips almost to the target line
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1901 ---
The reason i chosed that X point is that the gap in particular cases let you put it on the level of B point. But the main reason i prefer my waves is that in AB there isn't any "bump" that interrupt the down move, thing that i pretend in my waves to draw a correct XC (target) line.

Since it did not reach the target line, and there isn't any contrary wave, the wolfe waves have not been drawn correcly.

I could be wrong, i'm young so i'm willing to learn from a trader with more experience in wolfe wave than me

I think a lot of it is a personal choice for each trader but as I said the point needs to be at least somewhat distinct form the localized price action. Maybe a fractal, minor or major swing point.

--- 帖子 #1920 ---
Hi pet,

You have your wave backwards. There is no bearish WW. For a bearish WW with point X as your starting point, then point B and D would be making higher highs with D being the endpoint of the structure where price turns bearish.

There is actually a bullish WW in play here. Starting at point X, then B has made a lower low, the endpoint D would be a new lower low and the reversal point where price turns bullish.

Please see chart below

AUD/JPY
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1964 ---
Hi Kenny.

Yes I would leave them there. Once I locate a valid WW that has started on the D leg, I then map out the completed wave by finding where the AB=CD is located. That doesn't mean that price has to reach that level to make it a valid wave, it's just a level I want to have mapped out in advance. Now I can see if that level or zone has any confluence (pivots, fib levels, S/R, supply/demand zones, etc etc). In this way I can know in advance if the completion level may offer a higher edge of reversal if price reaches full AB=CD.

Having this done in advance lets me sit back and monitor price action as the D leg moves closer to the end point. Keeping an eye on the wave structure as far as symmetry as well as keeping an eye on the fundamentals/sentiment of the moment. If D is reached I am now prepared in advance to take action. Maybe I will be scaling in as the sweet zone is penetrated down towards point D. Or, maybe I will wait to monitor price action at point D and then enter after there is some sort of reversal confirmation.

Finding the WWs should be like riding a bike or chewing gum. Once you get to that stage, then you can use your filtering tools to find the WWs that provide the best edge. It's an individual endeavor. Each trader will have a different style/method of entering a trade. In many ways it's an art form and the chart is the canvas.

I look at the forex market as a living organism that lives and breathes based on the behavior of human beings. And all human beings, to some extent, are driven by fear and greed, especially in the forex market. Just remember that retail traders are the human prey and the market makers and big players are the predators. You must stay one step ahead at all times.

Be prepared, be patience, and above all else, be prudent with your capital. Without proper risk management it won't matter what strategy you are using.

Having NO position is still a position. The worst feeling in the world is chasing trades that aren't there and being so over leveraged that you have no available capital left to enter a trade when a golden opportunity arises.

Cheers, -Kurt

Here's a very basic process I go thru. Just the first layer of thinking. This is a WW that is 1000s of pips on GBP/JPY but a wave that I will keep stored and ready for future analysis and action if it remains valid.

Potential wave found and mapped out. You can use "parviz" WW indi which finds the AB=CD level for you, or use a modified ZIGZAG indi that shows the pips for each leg, or you can just measure AB manually and put a horizontal line where point D should be. I like to do that then put 2 triangles on my chart to keep it from being cluttered with to many lines. So here it is, very basic, all mapped out.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Now I zoom out just to have a look at the bigger picture. Of course looking left we see some interesting activity. I notice the 50FIB retracment is right there at the AB=CD level. Hmmm, coincidence? Could be, but certainly interesting considering we are talking about a move of over 7000 pips!! Anyways, we make note of this and look for more confluence on smaller time frames using multiple filtering tools if/when the WW gets near point D.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1971 ---
Hi Liquidsnake.

A couple of things:

1) The wave itself is valid but barely convergent, almost a perfect channel. I tend to stay away from these types. I like a deeper sweet zone with more convergence. The reversal point was about 200 pips beyond the AB=CD completion price.

2) I generally don't target the "target" line. It's certainly a reference point but a lot can happen on the way back down. Smaller counter waves may develop which may make me inclined to book some profits early as I tend to do anyways. But price not reaching the target line for me doesn't mean it was a failed WW

Cheers, -Kurt

--- 帖子 #2023 ---
Hi all,  asked Kurt about a ww on usdchf and eurnzd and how to behave if price bounce to B point, and how to manage position; and it's better to paste here the answer so probably can help many other as did to me:

"I move my SLs to BE depending on the volatility of the pair and how many pips it has moved. For a pair like EUR/NZD 9super volatile) I wouldn't likely move my stops after 15 pips in the green.

Also, I don't know how big your profit target is but If your trading 4H/DAILY on a pair like EUR/NZD then the TPs would be 200-400 pips at least so I would assume the SLs would be fairly big as well.

I tend to enter multiple positions and take profit on the first position if I make 20-30 pips. A lot though depends on the pair and the time frame.

Right now their is a bearish WW on EUR/NZD that is about 80 pips past the AB=CD level. I haven't entered because there is a lot of bullish momentum and this could possibly run another 500 pips plus upwards. Point is that the legs AB and CD are about 1700 pips each!! So its relative to how I would be setting my SLs and how I would go about booking profits."

Thank you Kurt!

--- 帖子 #2061 ---
after some tests, the biggest problem for WW trading is:

You can not focus on low spread currencies cause the signal appears everywhere.

Forex is a zero-sum game, if you trading sth with high spreads, you are working for your brokers.

--- 帖子 #2062 ---
In my broker there are pairs with very variable spreads ( at 23 p.m sometimes in some currencies arrive to 20-30 pips, so i have to remove it momentarily)

But i enter on any ww with my setup that i see; and i'm positive to think that in a random order the targets will be in a higher percentage than the SLs.

Second factor in my favor is the risk/reward, that is better than 1:1, sometimes cold reach even 1:5 or higher depending on your entry and your risk.

I see Forex a bit like this picture
Attached Image

So have to think in probabilities
