--- 帖子 #2085 ---
Hey Wolfe Wavers!!

Whether one celebrates Thanksgiving or not we all can find something to be thankful about. So I just wanted to say thank you to all of the posters here that have kept this thread alive. I have been extremely busy and haven't had much screen time lately.

Just to comment on the Gann fans and/or Pitchforks. As I stated in post one, this is a group effort that hopefully inspires traders to consider new and productive ways to filter out their potential trades. There's no right or wrong way. If your filters give you an edge and you use proper risk management then you will be a successful trader. Recently I have been testing/studying Fibonacci pivots (daily, weekly, monthly). I have found them to be a pretty powerful tool when coupled divergence (especially hidden divergence, i'e. trading with the trend)

Again thanks to all of the posters and please stay safe if you are travelling, especially in the US as Thanksgiving weekend is here along with the mindless insanity that we call the black Friday shopping event.

Building shorts here up to 7635. I think the Aussie may be exhausted in the short term. However, I wouldn't be surprised to see a low liquidity push north to wash out any weak shorts up to the 7635 area. I would think that level might be hard to break so my bias is still short.

--- 帖子 #2133 ---
Wolfe wave trading requires patience and conviction. Forex 101 says don't try to pick tops and bottoms. In essence, that's exactly what we are doing, at least on a localized basis. We aren't trying to predict some major shift in sentiment. We are only trying to capitalize on a temporary/localized market imbalance.

Example here. Why try and step in front of a speeding train. Well, for me, because the risk/reward is much more attractive. This is an aggressive entry. Many traders would rather wait for price action confirmation before entering, and that's fine and a good habit to get into. However, on smaller time frames, you may need a bigger SL, thus decreasing your risk reward. For bigger TFs, waiting for PA confirmation doesn't cut into your risk/reward as we would be looking for much larger moves anyways.

This may seem like playing with fire. I like fire, but I'm also a Pisces so I LOVE water and know when to douse the flames if the situation gets out of control

--- 帖子 #2147 ---
Hey mate I'm just curious where you get the fibo levels after the 161? I've never seen those levels used anywhere.

--- 帖子 #2148 ---
Well, I was searching for fixed levels for my entries and SL which I could use for steeper WWs too. Levels 113, 127.2 and 141.4 I got from this thread, which means from you.

Then I just thought I just add 100 to each of em and got levels 213, 227.2 and 241.4.

As for the levels in between I already got the 161.8 level, which is commonly used.

Then I went like this:

161.8 - 141.4 = 20.4

213 - 20.4 = 192.6

Then I finally added the 178.6 level cause it's kinda in the middle between 161.8 and 192.6 and because the 78.6 level is also a quite common fibo level, to which I just added 100.

I guess it's kinda odd, but I'm using those levels for a while now and it works quite well for me.

--- 帖子 #2149 ---
As long as it works that's good but they really have nothing to with the Fibonacci sequence and/or how the levels are derived. I was just curious because I never noticed them before until now.

--- 帖子 #2150 ---
Yeah, not really fibonacci canon, right? I just wanted some levels to use as something to hold on and it works for me more often as not.

Mabe I should call it the "Knurrem sequence".

--- 帖子 #2251 ---
Yes, sir.

You'll get trained to see with a little exercise. Just do it, doesn't take that much time. I tried a bunch of indicators but wasn't satisfied. You gotta trust in the skills and knowledge of somebody you most probably don't even know if you rely yourself on indicators.

But everything you need is already out there. As I said I use even the stoch just to confirm that the sweetspot supposedly is in extreme condition, that's it.

Mainly I use the bar-chart for the candlesticks distract from seeing the real pattern. Sometimes I switch even to line-chart to see what's really going on. You can draw Wolfe Waves on the line chart and they will work (although they look completely different if you switch the chart back to bars or candlesticks then), but they do work.

To me it seems it's all kind of dynamic anyways. Adjustable. And sometimes definitely needs some adjustment. Meaning sometimes it is not the highest high or lowest low points on the chart that needs to be connected (always close-by but not always top/bottom itself , just watch and check open/close also). Every now and then there may be a weird spike through one of the lines that still is not connected to the WW.

What are you using for the drawings? And how do you find them WWs?

--- 帖子 #2276 ---
Hi All. I've used Wolfe waves on and off in the past but have recently been looking at turning points at the 1.113 & 1.272 Fib levels and at the other end .113 & .272 levels. I've found that very often price will turn and/or stop and reverse again at the level at the other end. I've put a Fib across the last Wolfe Wave on GBUSD M30 chart as an example:-
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

I ran the fib from WW point 2 to WW point 3. As you can see, point 5 showed very strong up volume just above fib .113 and reversed, again with very strong volume, at 1.272

I hope someone finds this useful. I've found that those fib levels are often at turning points.

Thanks.

Mike
